星期文學會

論小品文 176

— 嫻女士

小品文是近代文學的寵兒，她受一羣文學者的歡愛。確實，她有被可愛的內在的力量的。允其是現在一般文學靑年，都在學習着小品文的寫作，小品文的被重視是無庸疑義的了。然而小品文的本質究竟怎樣？這一問題大概是每一個作者所想要理解的吧！

小品文是什麼？在國內已有許多學者論列過，但很難找得一個我們所能滿意的確當理解。

西洋文學中，對於這類文體的作品叫做Essay，也有採用美衛裏的所謂Sketch，作爲這一種文體的名稱的。Essay，周作人先生譯作「論文」，「美文」，實在不怎樣妥當。LF.Young曾對於文藝的Essay作過這樣的一段解釋：「文藝的Essay，介於小說作品與蛟嚴正的科學的哲學的論文之問，佔着一個利便的地位。牠是適應於任何的題目，應用一種暢快的，輕鬆的，顯豁的形式報告出來，並提出一種論點的檢討之範國，而是作者在任何題旨上發表思想的一種可愛慕的工具。」雖然他把小品文的性質解釋了一點，但對於小品文的整個認識還是不够的。

比較確當，要推夏丐尊先生的話：「從外形的長短上說，二三百字乃至千字以內的短文稱爲小品文。長文和小品文只是由外形而定。因此小品文的內容性質全然自由，可以叙事，可以含議論，可以抒情，可以寫景，毫不受何等的限制。……小品文，我國古來早已有了。如東坡小品就很有名。普通的所謂隨筆也可看作小品的一種。近來在各國小品文更盛行；並且體裁和我國向來的所謂小品文大不相同。現在的所謂小品文實即Sketch的譯語。大概都以片斷的文字表現實感或實生活的一部分的。」

馮三昧在小品文講話裏也有較精到的解釋：「所謂小品文就是指這內容單純外形短小的文字而言。小品文也可以叙事說理，但其本質實以抒情爲主。情之熱烈而深切的，可以造成種種的長篇大作，但是如果沒有這般熱切，而也是以代表實生活的一角的，想要將它保留下來不讓其貿然的消失，那麼，小品文眞是無上的工具了。小品文形式雖是散文，性質實近於詩歌。它不能像尋常文字那樣的　散，也不能像一般詩歌那樣的緊湊。如果散文詩外，還有介於詩歌與散文之間的中和地域，那它便是這地域上的一種新的花朶了。」

胡適之先生也有幾句可注意的話，他說：「用平淡的談話，包藏著深刻的意味，有時」很像笨拙，其實確是滑稽。」這裏所說的滑稽似乎頗多語病，也落於淺薄，宜改爲幽默或諧趣，因爲幽默和諧趣都是小品文裏應具的條件。　綜合起來說，應得下面一個較完美的結論：小品文是以精悍的諧趣的雋永的文字，輕快的技巧，表現和批評人生之一角或片斷的實感的短文。

小品文在文藝的園地裹是幽默的一個僻境，並不像古人所說的那麼寬廣和遼闊，鐘敬文先生曾說：「……古人於小品云云，似指的是些篇幅不長的文章，其體裁兼有論說，序跋，傳記，銘誌等，內容則寫景，叙事，抒情，議論都齊備。依此，實和平常所謂文章沒有什麼分別，只是短篇罷了。」

小品文不就是短篇，小品文自有風格上的特徵。日本作家廚川白村在他的出了象牙之塔一書中說：「如果是冬天，便坐暖爐旁邊的安樂椅子上，倘在夏天，便披浴衣，啜香茗，隨隨便便，和好友任性閒話，將這　話照樣地移在紙上的東西就是Essay興之所至，也說些不至於頭痛的道理，也有冷嘲，也有警句，旣有Humor（滑稽），也有Pathoo（感奮），所談的題目，天下國家的大事不待言，還有市井的瑣事，書籍的批評，相識者的消息，以及自己過去的追懷，想到什麼就縱談到什麼，而託於即興之筆者，是這一類文章。」，這已很足够說明小品文的風格及其題材的來源了。

這里我們得將小品文與其他文藝作品作一個比較：

一·小品文與詩歌　小品文雖常富有抒情的抒述，就是那一種富有詩意的小品文。但詩畢竟不就是小品文，詩是依據韻律爲必要條件的，小品文則吾。

二•小品文與小說小品與小說，從牠們的結構，表現方法各方面都可分別出牠們的差異。小說從攝取題材之後，須經過相當布局，有嚴格的結構，人物，背景，對話，叙事，都曾經過了一番推敲，然後用經濟的技巧表現出來的。小品則不然，上面已經說過，牠是用「即興」的方法來表現其合于目的的人生之一角；牠的結構不能如小說一樣嚴格。

三•小品與論說文　小品有時也是事理或意象方面的論說。有不少小品文是以冷冽嚴峻的筆鋒針對着某一事理之正面，或以冷嘲熱諷的口吻從側面輕敲側擊，讀者覺得另有一種淸寒的氣息襲人肺腑。但小品文到底不就是論說文，因爲牠仍然根據于牠即興的技術的，並沒有嚴正的結構使成論說文應具的形式。

四•小品文與戲劇　有時小品文作者也利用戲劇的形式和簡單的對話方法，來完成他小品文的抒寫，但這樣的例子却很少。例如陳衡哲女士的運河與揚子江，我們始終認爲是一篇品文，沒有當牠爲戲劇。

五•小品文與日記　普通小品文的形式，出于閒話或隨筆的體例的，要算最多，但有一種特殊的形式！日記與書信

Page 23

，也佔着重要的位置。郁達夫先生說：日記文學是文學里的一個核心，是正統以外的一個寳藏。日記小品之所以感人極深，正因爲她是眞情的流露，用不着做作，她是渾樸無　的白璧。

六•小品文與書信書信體的小品文也是文學中的珍品。周作人先生說日記和尺牘是文學中特別有趣味的東西，因爲比別的文章更鮮明地表出作者的個性。冰心女士的寄小讀者，溫柔綺麗的辭藻，天眞濃部的情精，許多讀者都爲之愛不釋手，他如郭沫若田漢宗白華三人的三葉集，他們如何討論着人生問題呢？剛直，雄偉，哀婉，充滿了熱烈緊張的情緒，也是很好的小品文。

七·小品文與散文詩　在某一種情形下，小品文與散文詩簡直沒有清晰的境界可分。我們很知道有不少小品文中含有十分的詩意，而構造形式也並不怎樣異於散文詩，木村毅說：「不可忘了散文能夠有今日之發達，有不少地方借用了」詩的工夫和技巧。」木村毅曾舉了一個詩與散文的境界的例子：　終日；　從朝到晚；　從掛着朝霧的時候起到蟋蟀鳴的時候止。　　只能表現日常一切的簡明事態，不能當作傳達特殊思想感情的表現。　的表現，就進到了一個另外的世界了。牠並不直接表現內容，而以暗示的方法使讀者自己去把握潛藏於記述的底蘿的內容。小品文是適用（三）的表現的，牠需要色彩的渲染，趣味的濃厚，以及文學的情趣。所以我們可說小品文是「詩的散文」。

這里我們想肘論小品文對於多數作者的貢獻及其內在價値之估計：

第一，對於作者的價値

甲，培養技衛——要成爲一個技衛成熟的作家，開始不能立即寫作長篇或巨製，長篇或巨製是較繁重的工作；小品文取材旣容易，構造又輕便，經過相當時期的練習，技衛自然靈活了。

乙，開拓思路——從日常生活里描繪人生之一角，作者因實感的寫作，興趣橫生，文思如幽谷之淸泉，源源不絕。

丙，增加生活的吟味能力——文學的能事是表現人生，是批評人生。小品文同樣是實生活的表現與批評。故要作小品文，一定要吟味自己的實生活，理解自己實生活的情趣，然後才能表現生活。

丁，養成敏銳的觀察力！—文學的表現是深刻的人生橫心的發掘，我們應養成敏銳的透視生活或社會各階層，衡量自我的理想。

第二，內在價値之估計

甲，自我色彩之擴展——這里不一定是冷酷的呆板的客觀記錄，而是另一種極濃重的個性調子在彈奏着。

乙，剎那浮現之執着——當人類的息想與情緒剎那的浮現時，把牠把握住，從我們這簡短的小品中不放走這剎那的甜蜜。

總之，小品文不是載道的大文章，不是無病的呻吟，而是一切人生社會宇宙之正面或側面之寫照，是技衛宮中的一件珍物。

言論

想到麥唐納和赫理歐的下塲 177

— 吉仁

當麥唐納在英國落選，與跟着來的法國赫理歐失掉急進社會黨黨魁地位的消息傳出援，在一個外國雜誌上曾刋出了一幅富有諷刺意味的漫畫。那漫畫所表現的是麥唐納的狼狽下台，赫理歐打着一把洋傘，狼狽地緊跟在麥唐納的屁設援面，走上同一的途徑。我看了這樣的漫畫之後，自然覺得好笑，但同時更使我不能不佩服作畫者腦筋的靈活，他能那樣無情地嘲笑了在英法政治舞台上專門賣野人頭的兩個政客所遭的悲慘的命運。

麥唐納本來是英國的工黨領袖，他曾利用過英國一部份工人的力量，作了兩次工黨內閣的首相；一般看凍，可說是英國政治舞台上最活躍的人物之一了。但在一九三一年當英國在財政上發生空前的困難時，麥廣納爲了英帝國主義的安寗，圖謀打開財政難關，竟不情公然離開他自己的工黨，與保守黨相勾結，伏貼在鮑爾溫的懷抱里。這樣一來，當然要爲他所屬的工黨所唾棄，爲原來尚對他抱有好戚的一部份英國人所恥笑，結果是在這屆英國的選舉中大受選民的責罵，竟自落了選。援來雖然由於鮑爾溫的可憐他，在現在英國內閣中得了一個位置，但從今以後，這位曾經出過大風頭的政客的政治生命便算完了，他的眞面目已完全顯露了出來，他將不能再欺屬他所欺騙過的人羣了；他的命運只有終身待奉鮑爾溫，或者爲英國人民拋棄在廢物堆里，從此湮沒無聞！

至於赫理歐，也是法國頂有名的人物。他原是法國最大政黨——急進社會一黨的黨魁；曾任法國內閣總理；從一九〇五年起他就關始任里昻市長，一直繼續到現在，法國人呼之爲「市長之王」；這當然可說是近年來法國政治舞臺上最紅的人物了。但當賴伐爾內閣時，他便首先違背急進社會黨的意志，支持賴伐爾違反民意的政策，結果引起了自己黨的反對，被迫辭去黨魁的地位。這便是一他走上麥唐納所走的道路第一步的表現一。最近法國衆議院選舉初决揭曉，「出人意表」的赫理歐竟告落選，據說這是「法國歷史上的創見」。自然，他在這决選舉中的命運，還要在五月三日的第二次投票中才能完全確定，但這决初選的失敗總是法國人民在繼續給與他的敎訓，總是他的政治地位在繼續下落的表現；卽使在第二决投票中他僥倖當選了，那也不過是他在作最後的掙扎，在維持其殘餘的政治生命而已。不過，據報載，赫理歐在初選失敗後，已聲明「現擬退出政治，不再爲第二决選舉之候選人」；若然，那我們可以說赫理歐還算能「識時務」，能在人民對己不滿時不繼續戀棧，這此較起已經失敗了的麥唐納還要去乞憐鮑爾溫以維持一個官職的事來，可說是較勝一籌了。然而，不管怎樣，這兩位人物的命運總是一樣的。

由麥唐納和赫理歐所遭到的同一命運，使我們發生了兩個重要的感想；

第一，麥唐納本質上是改良主義，自由主義者。這樣的人物只能緩和現寳的生活爭鬬，根本就不能走上前進的道路；在某種情形下，他甚至可能去幹公然開倒車的勾當。所以，麥唐納當其還能繼續起欺騙的緩和作用時，他還可戴着改良的面具，努力和平的說敎；但是，現在”也不能起這樣的緩和作用了，他所領導的黨員已日益離開他而去走自已應走的道路了，因之他爲了自己個人的官位，便自動地撕去了他的面具，公然與保守黨勾結起來，去努力開倒車的工作。同時，赫理歐，也是保守的中間的自由主義者，他過去所領導的急進社會黨雖然有「急進」之名，但實際上却是法國市民的中間政黨。由於法國在上决大戰中得到了許多勝利品，社會比較安定，所以這個中間的法國市民政黨——社會急進黨所有的中間的溫和保守的政見，便獲得了多數法國人民的贊助，使這政黨成爲了法國最大的政黨，而這政黨的黨魁赫理歐也就成爲了法國政治上最出風頭的人物了。但最近法國因爲內外危機的發展，左右兩極端鬥爭的尖銳，中間的急進社會黨已逐漸失勢，連時代的尾巴都跟不上的那樣的赫理歐，在這法國的大時代中當然會要援退，甚至去與最保守的勢力結合，這是必然的。——依據這個分析，我們可以想到如像麥唐納和赫理歐那樣的人是最靠不住的：我們在結交朋友中，在社會活動中，應該餒密防備他們，以免被地們拍賣。

第二，麥唐納曾是英國工黨的領袖，赫理歐曾是法國急進社會黨的黨魁，他們過去的政治地位是他們的黨所給與，並不是他們個人創造出來的，所以，一旦他們背叛了自己黨的立塲，違反了自己黨的意志，也就同時喪失了他們固有的力量和地位。由此我們更可以想到入是社會的，集團的動物，個人的力量要在集團中才能生長，才能發揮，因而個人的出路也只有在集團的出路中才能找到，誰離開了他自己的集團而又找不到新的更好的集團參加，只是去獨行獨幹，或者依附於人，那是只有繼續使自己的靈魂墮落，走進沒有出路的牛角尖端的。麥唐納與赫埋歐之離開和違背他們的政黨，就斷送了自己的政治生命，甘地之從印度的民族解放運動中退却下來，便更快地喪失了他在印度人民中的威望，股汝耕等的叛國是遭到了全中國人民的唾駡，……這類的例子眞是舉不勝舉。

名人訪問記

唐槐秋先生 178

— 徐心芹

凡留心中國新與話劇運動的人，都是知道南國劇社的歷史價値的吧？而南國社的領袖演員話劇前輩唐大哥，那更是任何人要喊了聲「久仰」的。最近，唐槐秋所領導的「中國旅行劇團」已經從華北載譽歸來了，記者聞訊後，便特往竦斐德路穎邨十三號訪問這位唐大哥。

到了穎邨，只見弄堂內過街樓下堆着大批佈景，跟蹤着那佈景曲折着走到十三號，在門外便聽見門內念台詞的聲音，都是一派淸脆的北平腔調。而忽然，有一個中年人的狂笑山遠而近地到了門口。這時，正好我推鬥了，他開門，幾乎撞了一個滿懷。我一看便很驚喜地喊出：「好久不看見了！店…」他很興奮地用手來握着我的手：「呀！你們的消息眞靈通，今天已經來了三四回探問消息的人了。請進來坐!」

以下接第五版

1936.05.03

The Legislative Yuan Passes the Draft Constitution of the Republic of China 1

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 59th meeting on the 1st, passing the revised draft of the Constitution of the Republic of China. The original text is as follows:

The National Assembly of the Republic of China, entrusted by all the people, following the teachings of Mr. Sun Yat-sen, the founder of the Republic of China, hereby establishes this Constitution, promulgates it throughout the country, and pledges eternal adherence.

Chapter I: General Principles

Article 1: The Republic of China is a Republic based on the Three Principles of the People.

Article 2: The sovereignty of the Republic of China belongs to the entire citizenry.

Article 3: Those possessing the nationality of the Republic of China are citizens of the Republic of China.

Article 4: The territory of the Republic of China consists of the inherent territories of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, Xikang, Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Qinghai, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Xinjiang, Mongolia, Tibet, etc.

The territory of the Republic of China may not be altered without a resolution by the National Assembly.

Article 5: All ethnic groups within the Republic of China are equal constituent elements of the Chinese nation.

Article 6: The national flag of the Republic of China is designated as a red field with a white sun in a blue sky in the upper left corner.

Article 7: The capital of the Republic of China is established in Nanjing.

Chapter II: Rights and Duties of the People

Article 8: All people of the Republic of China are equal under the law.

Article 9: The people have the freedom of person. They may not be arrested, detained, interrogated, or punished except in accordance with the law.

When a person is arrested or detained on suspicion of a crime, the executing authority shall immediately inform the person and their relatives of the reasons for the arrest or detention and transfer them to the competent court for interrogation within twenty-four hours at the latest. The person or another person may also petition the competent court to issue a writ of habeas corpus to the executing authority within twenty-four hours.

The court shall not refuse the aforementioned petition, and the executing authority shall not refuse the court's writ of habeas corpus.

Article 10: The people shall not be subject to military trial, except for active-duty military personnel.

Article 11: The people have the freedom of residence, and their place of residence may not be entered, searched, or sealed except in accordance with the law.

Article 12: The people have the freedom of movement, and it may not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 13: The people have the freedom of speech, writing, and publication, and it may not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 14: The people have the freedom of secret communication, and it may not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 15: The people have the freedom of religious belief, and it may not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 16: The people have the freedom of assembly and association, and it may not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 17: The property of the people may not be requisitioned, levied, searched, or confiscated except in accordance with the law.

Article 18: The people have the right to petition, appeal, and litigate in accordance with the law.

Article 19: The people have the right to elect, recall, initiate, and referendum in accordance with the law.

Article 20: The people have the right to take examinations in accordance with the law.

Article 21: The people have the duty to pay taxes in accordance with the law.

Article 22: The people have the duty to perform military service and corvée in accordance with the law.

Article 23: The people have the duty to perform public service in accordance with the law.

Article 24: All other freedoms and rights of the people that do not harm social order or public interest shall be protected by the Constitution and may not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 25: Laws restricting the freedoms or rights of the people shall be limited to what is necessary to safeguard national security, avert emergencies, maintain social order, or promote public interest.

Article 26: Any public official who illegally infringes upon the freedom or rights of the people shall be held criminally and civilly liable, in addition to disciplinary action in accordance with the law. The injured person may also seek compensation from the state in accordance with the law for the damage suffered.

Chapter III: The National Assembly

Article 27: The National Assembly shall be composed of the following National Representatives: Each county, city, and equivalent area shall elect one representative, but for every 500,000 people exceeding 300,000, one additional representative shall be elected. County and city equivalent areas shall be defined by law. The number of representatives elected from Mongolia and Tibet shall be determined by law. The number of representatives elected by citizens residing abroad shall be determined by law.

Article 28: The election of National Representatives shall be conducted by universal, equal, direct, and secret ballot.

Article 29: Citizens of the Republic of China who have reached the age of twenty shall have the right to elect representatives in accordance with the law, and those who have reached the age of twenty-five shall have the right to be elected as representatives in accordance with the law.

Article 30: The term of office for National Representatives shall be six years.

National Representatives who violate the law or are derelict in their duties may be recalled by their original electoral district in accordance with the law.

Article 31: The National Assembly shall be convened by the President once every three years for a session of one month, which may be extended by one month if necessary.

The National Assembly may convene a temporary National Assembly on its own initiative with the consent of two-fifths or more of the representatives.

The President may convene a temporary National Assembly.

The meeting place of the National Assembly shall be in the location of the central government.

Article 32: The powers of the National Assembly are as follows: To elect the President, Vice President, President of the Legislative Yuan, Vice President of the Legislative Yuan, President of the Control Yuan, Vice President of the Control Yuan, members of the Legislative Yuan, and members of the Control Yuan. To recall the President, Vice President, Presidents and Vice Presidents of the Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuans, members of the Legislative Yuan, and members of the Control Yuan. To initiate laws. To referendum laws. To amend the Constitution. Other powers conferred by the Constitution.

Article 33: National Representatives shall not be held responsible externally for their speeches and votes made during meetings.

Article 34: Except for flagrant offenses, National Representatives may not be arrested or detained during the session without the permission of the National Assembly.

Article 35: The organization of the National Assembly, the election and recall of National Representatives, and the procedures for the National Assembly to exercise it's powers shall be determined by law.

Chapter IV: The Central Government

Section I: The President

Article 36: The President is the head of state and represents the Republic of China externally.

Article 37: The President commands the national land, sea, and air forces.

Article 38: The President promulgates laws and issues orders in accordance with the law, with the countersignature of the head of the relevant Yuan.

Article 39: The President exercises the power to declare war, make peace, and conclude treaties in accordance with the law.

Article 40: The President declares and lifts martial law in accordance with the law.

Article 41: The President exercises the power to grant amnesties, pardons, commutation of sentences, and restoration of rights in accordance with the law.

Article 42: The President appoints and removes civil and military officials in accordance with the law.

Article 43: The President confers honors in accordance with the law.

Article 44: When the nation encounters an emergency or a major economic crisis that requires rapid action, the President may, with the resolution of the Executive Council, issue emergency decrees and take necessary measures, but shall submit them to the Legislative Yuan for ratification within three months after the issuance of the decrees.

Article 45: The President may convene the heads of the five Yuans to consult on matters involving two or more Yuans, and on matters for presidential consultation.

Article 46: The President is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 47: Citizens of the Republic of China who have reached the age of forty may be elected as President or Vice President.

Article 48: The election of the President and Vice President shall be determined by law.

Article 49: The terms of office for the President and Vice President shall be six years each, and they may be re-elected for one consecutive term.

Article 50: The President shall take the following oath on the day of inauguration:

"I solemnly swear to the people with sincerity and good faith that I will abide by the Constitution, faithfully perform my duties, promote the welfare of the people, and defend the nation, without failing the trust of the people. If I violate this oath, I am willing to be severely punished by the national law. I solemnly swear."

Article 51: When the office of the President is vacant, the Vice President shall succeed to the office. When the President is unable to perform their duties due to illness, the Vice President shall act on their behalf. When both the President and Vice President are unable to perform their duties, the President of the Executive Yuan shall act on their behalf.

Article 52: The President shall relinquish their office on the day their term expires. If the next President has not yet been elected or if neither the President nor the Vice President has assumed office after the election, the President of the Executive Yuan shall act as President.

Article 53: The President of the Executive Yuan acting as President shall not exceed six months.

Article 54: The President, except for offenses of treason or insurrection, shall not be subject to criminal prosecution without being impeached or removed from office.

Section II: The Executive Yuan

Article 55: The Executive Yuan is the highest organ of the central government exercising executive power.

Article 56: The Executive Yuan shall have one President and one Vice President, and several Ministers of State, who shall be appointed and removed by the President.

The number of Ministers of State mentioned in the preceding paragraph who do not head ministries shall not exceed half of the number of those who head ministries as stipulated in paragraph 1 of Article 58.

Article 57: The Executive Yuan shall establish ministries and commissions to administer executive powers.

Article 58: The Ministers of each ministry and the chairpersons of each commission of the Executive Yuan shall be appointed by the President from among the Ministers of State.

Article 59: The President, Vice President, Ministers of State, Ministers of each ministry, and chairpersons of each commission of the Executive Yuan are each responsible to the President.

Article 60: The Executive Yuan shall establish an Executive Council, which shall be composed of the President, Vice President, and Ministers of State of the Executive Yuan, with the President of the Executive Yuan as chairperson.

Article 61: The following matters shall be resolved by the Executive Council: Legislative bills and budget proposals submitted to the Legislative Yuan. Cases of martial law and amnesty submitted to the Legislative Yuan. Cases of declaration of war, peace negotiations, and treaty proposals submitted to the Legislative Yuan, as well as other proposals concerning important international matters. Matters of common concern among the ministries and commissions. Matters submitted for deliberation by the President or the President of the Executive Yuan. Matters proposed by the Vice President, Ministers of State, ministers of each ministry, and chairpersons of each commission of the Executive Yuan.

Article 62: The organization of the Executive Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section III: The Legislative Yuan

Article 63: The Legislative Yuan is the highest organ of the central government exercising legislative power and is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 64: The Legislative Yuan has the power to resolve legislative bills, budget proposals, cases of martial law, amnesty, declaration of war, peace negotiations, and treaty proposals, as well as other matters concerning important international affairs.

Article 65: Regarding legislative matters, the Legislative Yuan may raise questions to all Yuans, ministries, and commissions.

Article 66: The Legislative Yuan shall have one President and one Vice President, with a term of three years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 67: Members of the Legislative Yuan shall be pre-elected by National Representatives elected from each province, Mongolia, Tibet, and citizens residing abroad, and a list of candidates shall be submitted to the National Assembly for election according to the following quotas, and the candidates shall not be limited to National Representatives:

Each province with a population of less than five million: four members per province. Provinces with a population of five million or more but less than ten million: six members per province. Provinces with a population of ten million or more but less than fifteen million: eight members per province. Provinces with a population of fifteen million or more but less than twenty million: ten members per province. Provinces with a population of twenty million or more but less than twenty-five million: twelve members per province. Provinces with a population of twenty-five million or more but less than thirty million: fourteen members per province. Provinces with a population of thirty million or more: sixteen members per province.

Mongolia and Tibet: eight members each.

Citizens residing abroad: eight members.

Article 68: The term of office for members of the Legislative Yuan is three years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 69: The Executive, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuans may submit proposals to the Legislative Yuan regarding matters under their jurisdiction.

Article 70: The President may submit resolutions of the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration before they are promulgated or implemented.

When the Legislative Yuan maintains the original resolution with the approval of two-thirds or more of the members present regarding a proposal submitted for reconsideration, the President shall immediately promulgate or implement it, but in the case of legislative bills and treaty proposals, a referendum by the National Assembly may be requested.

Article 71: The President shall promulgate resolutions of the Legislative Yuan submitted for promulgation within thirty days after the arrival of the resolution.

Article 72: Members of the Legislative Yuan shall not be held responsible externally for their speeches and votes within the Yuan.

Article 73: Except for flagrant offenses, members of the Legislative Yuan may not be arrested or detained without the permission of the Legislative Yuan.

Article 74: Members of the Legislative Yuan may not concurrently hold other public offices or engage in business.

Article 75: The election of members of the Legislative Yuan and the organization of the Legislative Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section IV: The Judicial Yuan

Article 76: The Judicial Yuan is the highest organ of the central government exercising judicial power, administering civil, criminal, and administrative litigation trials, and judicial administration.

Article 77: The Judicial Yuan shall have one President and one Vice President, with a term of three years, who shall be appointed by the President.

The President of the Judicial Yuan is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 78: Matters concerning amnesty, commutation of sentences, and restoration of rights shall be submitted by the President of the Judicial Yuan to the President for execution in accordance with the law.

Article 79: The Judicial Yuan has the power to interpret laws and orders uniformly.

Article 80: Judges shall conduct trials independently according to the law.

Article 81: Judges may not be dismissed without being subject to criminal punishment, disciplinary action, or a declaration of interdiction. They may not be suspended from office, transferred, or have their salaries reduced except in accordance with the law.

Article 82: The organization of the Judicial Yuan and the organization of courts at all levels shall be determined by law.

Section V: The Examination Yuan

Article 83: The Examination Yuan is the highest organ of the central government exercising examination power, administering examinations and appointments.

Article 84: The Examination Yuan shall have one President and one Vice President, with a term of three years, who shall be appointed by the President.

The President of the Examination Yuan is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 85: The following qualifications shall be determined by the Examination Yuan through examinations and appointments in accordance with the law: Qualifications for civil service appointments. Qualifications for candidates for public office. Qualifications for practicing specialized professions and technical personnel.

Article 86: The organization of the Examination Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section VI: The Control Yuan

Article 87: The Control Yuan is the highest organ of the central government exercising control power, administering impeachment, censure, and auditing, and is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 88: The Control Yuan may raise questions to all Yuans, ministries, and commissions in accordance with the law in order to exercise its power of control.

Article 89: The Control Yuan shall have one President and one Vice President, with a term of three years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 90: Members of the Control Yuan shall be pre-elected by National Representatives elected from each province, Mongolia, Tibet, and citizens residing abroad, with two candidates pre-elected from each region, and submitted to the National Assembly for election. The candidates shall not be limited to National Representatives.

Article 91: The term of office for members of the Control Yuan is three years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 92: When central and local government officials violate the law or are derelict in their duties, the Control Yuan may propose an impeachment case with the proposal of one or more members of the Control Yuan and the decision of five or more members of the Control Yuan. However, impeachment cases against the President, Vice President, and Presidents and Vice Presidents of the Executive, Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuans must be proposed by ten or more members of the Control Yuan and decided by a review of more than one-half of all members of the Control Yuan before they can be submitted.

Article 93: Impeachment cases against the President, Vice President, and Presidents and Vice Presidents of the Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuans, after being established in accordance with the provisions of the preceding article, shall be submitted to the National Assembly. During the adjournment of the National Assembly, the National Representatives shall be requested to convene a temporary National Assembly in accordance with the law to resolve whether to remove them from their positions.

Article 94: Members of the Control Yuan shall not be held responsible externally for their speeches and votes within the Yuan.

Article 95: Except for flagrant offenses, members of the Control Yuan may not be arrested or detained without the permission of the Control Yuan.

Article 96: Members of the Control Yuan may not concurrently hold other public offices or engage in business.

Article 97: The election of members of the Control Yuan and the organization of the Control Yuan shall be determined by law.

Chapter V: Local Government

Section I: Provinces

Article 98: Provinces shall establish provincial governments to implement central government laws and supervise local autonomy.

Article 99: Provincial governments shall have one governor, with a term of three years, who shall be appointed and removed by the central government.

Article 100: Provinces shall establish provincial councils. Each county and city shall have one councillor, elected by the county and city councils, with a term of three years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 101: The organization of provincial governments, the organization and powers of provincial councils, and the election and recall of provincial councillors shall be determined by law.

Article 102: The political system of areas that have not yet established provinces shall be determined by law.

Section II: Counties

Article 103: Counties are units of local autonomy.

Article 104: Matters that are by their nature suited to local conditions shall be classified as matters of local autonomy.

Matters of local autonomy shall be determined by law.

Article 105: County residents shall exercise the powers of initiation and referendum on matters of county autonomy in accordance with the law, and shall exercise the powers of election and recall over county magistrates and other county autonomous personnel in accordance with the law.

Article 106: Counties shall establish county councils, with councillors elected by the county assembly, with a term of three years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 107: County regulations that conflict with central laws or provincial regulations shall be invalid.

Article 108: Counties shall establish county governments, with one county magistrate, elected by the county assembly. The President, Vice President of the Executive Yuan, may be re-elected, with a term of three years.

Candidates for county magistrate shall be limited to those who have passed the central examination or appointment qualifications.

Article 109: County magistrates shall handle county autonomy and be subject to the direction of the provincial governor, and shall execute matters delegated by the central and provincial governments.

Article 110: The organization and powers of county councils, the election and recall of county councillors, the organization of county governments, and the election and recall of county magistrates shall be determined by law.

Section III: Cities

Article 111: The provisions concerning counties shall apply mutatis mutandis to city autonomy, except as otherwise provided in this section.

Article 112: Cities shall establish city councils, with councillors elected by the city assembly, with one-third of the councillors re-elected each year.

Article 113: Cities shall establish city governments, with one mayor, elected by the city assembly, with a term of three years, and they may be re-elected. Candidates for mayor shall be limited to those who have passed the central examination or appointment qualifications.

Article 114: Mayors shall handle city autonomy and be subject to the direction of the supervisory authority, and shall execute matters delegated by the central or provincial governments.

Article 115: The organization and powers of city councils, the election and recall of city councillors, the organization of city governments, and the election and recall of mayors shall be determined by law.

Chapter VI: National Economy

Article 116: The economic system of the Republic of China shall be based on the Principle of People's Livelihood to ensure the equitable sufficiency of the people's livelihood.

Article 117: Land within the territory of the Republic of China belongs to the entire citizenry. The ownership of land acquired by the people in accordance with the law shall be protected and restricted by law.

The state may tax or levy land owned by the people in accordance with the declared or government-assessed land value in accordance with the law.

Landowners shall be obligated to fully utilize the land they own.

Article 118: Minerals attached to the land and natural resources that can be economically utilized by the public belong to the state and are not affected by the people's acquisition of land ownership.

Article 119: Land value that increases without the application of labor or capital shall be appropriated for public enjoyment by the people through the imposition of a land value increment tax.

Article 120: The state shall, in the distribution and reorganization of land, adhere to the principle of supporting owner-cultivators and those who use the land themselves.

Article 121: When the state deems that private wealth and private enterprises hinder the balanced development of the people's livelihood, it may regulate them in accordance with the law.

Article 122: The state shall encourage, guide, and protect the people's productive enterprises and foreign trade.

Article 123: Public utilities and other monopolistic enterprises shall be operated by the state in principle, but may be privately operated with special permission when necessary.

In the event of an urgent national defense need, the state may temporarily manage privately operated enterprises granted special permission as described in the preceding paragraph, and may nationalize them in accordance with the law.

However, appropriate compensation shall be provided.

Article 124: The state shall implement policies to protect labor in order to improve the living standards of workers, enhance their productive skills, and relieve unemployment.

Women and children engaged in labor shall be given special protection according to their age and physical condition.

Article 125: Labor and management shall develop productive enterprises based on the principles of coordination and mutual assistance.

Article 126: The state shall enrich the rural economy, improve rural life, and improve the efficiency of farmers' farming through scientific methods in order to promote agricultural development and the welfare of farmers.

The state may regulate the types, quantities, and distribution of agricultural products.

Article 127: The state shall provide appropriate relief or compensation to people who are disabled or die as a result of military service, corvée, or public service.

Article 128: The state shall provide appropriate relief to the elderly, the weak, the disabled, and those unable to support themselves.

Article 129: The following matters shall be resolved by the Legislative Yuan at the central level. If they can be handled by provincial or county regulations in accordance with the law, they shall be resolved by the statutory organs of each level. The establishment of taxes, levies, fees, fines, penalties, or other compulsory income, and changes in their collection rates. The raising of public debt, the disposal of public property, or the conclusion of contracts that increase the burden on the public treasury. The establishment or abolition of public monopolies or other profit-making enterprises. The granting or revocation of monopolies or other privileges.

Provincial and county governments may not raise foreign debt or directly utilize foreign capital without special authorization by law.

Article 130: All goods within the territory of the Republic of China shall be allowed to circulate freely, and may not be prohibited except in accordance with the law.

Customs duties are central government revenue and shall be levied on goods entering and leaving the country, limited to once.

Governments at all levels shall not levy domestic transit taxes on goods.

The power to levy all taxes and levies on goods belongs to the central government and may not be exercised except in accordance with the law.

Chapter VII: Education

Article 131: The purpose of education in the Republic of China is to promote the national spirit, cultivate national morality, train self-governing ability, and enhance life skills in order to create healthy citizens.

Article 132: All people of the Republic of China shall have equal educational opportunities.

Article 133: All public and private educational institutions throughout the country shall be subject to state supervision and shall be responsible for implementing the state's educational policies.

Article 134: All school-age children between the ages of six and twelve shall receive basic education free of tuition.

Article 135: All people who have exceeded the age limit but have not received basic education shall receive remedial education free of tuition.

Article 136: The establishment of national universities and national vocational schools shall focus on the needs of the region in order to maintain equal opportunities for people in all regions to enjoy higher education and to promote the balanced development of national culture.

Article 137: The minimum amount of educational expenditure shall be 15 percent of the total budget at the central level and 10 percent of the total budget at the provincial and county levels. Independent educational funds in accordance with the law shall also be guaranteed.

Educational expenditure in impoverished provinces and regions shall be subsidized by the national treasury.

Article 138: The state shall reward or subsidize the following enterprises and people: Private educational enterprises in the country that have achieved excellent results. Educational enterprises of citizens residing abroad. Those who have made inventions in academic technology. Those who have been engaged in education for a long time with excellent results. Students who excel in both conduct and studies but are unable to continue their education.

Chapter VIII: Implementation and Amendment of the Constitution

Article 139: The term "law" in the Constitution refers to laws passed by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the President.

Article 140: Laws that conflict with the Constitution shall be invalid. Whether a law conflicts with the Constitution shall be determined by the Judicial Yuan upon the proposal of the Control Yuan within six months after the law's implementation. The details shall be determined by law.

Article 141: Orders that conflict with the Constitution or laws shall be invalid.

Article 142: The interpretation of the Constitution shall be made by the Judicial Yuan.

Article 143: Before more than half of the provinces and regions in the country have completed local autonomy, members of the Legislative Yuan and members of the Control Yuan shall be elected and appointed in accordance with the following provisions:

Members of the Legislative Yuan shall be pre-elected by National Representatives elected from each province, Mongolia, Tibet, and citizens residing abroad, with one-half pre-elected in accordance with the quotas stipulated in Article 67, and submitted to the National Assembly for election. The remaining half shall be nominated by the President of the Legislative Yuan and appointed by the President.

Members of the Control Yuan shall be pre-elected by National Representatives elected from each province, Mongolia, Tibet, and citizens residing abroad, with one-half pre-elected in accordance with the quotas stipulated in Article 90, and submitted to the National Assembly for election. The remaining half shall be nominated by the President of the Control Yuan and appointed by the President.

Article 144: In counties where local autonomy has not been completed, the county magistrate shall be be appointed and removed by the central government. The provisions of the preceding paragraph shall apply mutatis Mutandis to cities where autonomy has not been completed.

Article 145: The procedures for promoting local autonomy shall be determined by law.

Article 146: The powers of the first National Assembly shall be exercised by the National Assembly that formulated the Constitution.

Article 147: The Constitution may not be amended except by the proposal of more than one-fourth of all representatives of the National Assembly, the attendance of more than three-fourths, and the resolution of more than two-thirds of the representatives present.

Proposals to amend the Constitution shall be announced by the proposers one year before the meeting of the National Assembly.

Article 148: Matters stipulated in the Constitution for which it is necessary to separately establish implementation procedures shall be determined by law. (Central News Agency electric dispatch)

The Legislative Yuan Passes the National Assembly Representative Election Law: Allocation of Quotas Follows Central Principles; Overseas Chinese from the United States and the Philippines Each Receive One Additional Seat; Northeastern Provinces Included in Special Elections 2

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan convened its 59th meeting on the morning of the 2nd and continued deliberation on the National Assembly Representative Election Law. Sixty-one committee members were present, with Sun Ke presiding. The full text of the bill, consisting of 62 articles and four appendices, was read, revised, and passed in the third reading. However, regarding the division of electoral districts in various provinces in Appendix 2, Liu Guanxun, Zhang Weihan, Yang Gongda, and others had proposed amendments to the provinces of Shanxi, Yunnan, and Sichuan. The Yuan authorized a 24-member committee, including Lin Bin, Huang Youchang, Shi Weihuan, Lu Zhiyi, and Xu Yuangao, who had drafted the initial version, to consult with the internal representatives, reorganize the draft, and submit it directly to the President for approval and then to the National Government for promulgation. Fu Bingchang had already reported the drafting process in detail on the 1st. Lin Bin had also explained the allocation of representative quotas on the 1st, stating that the allocation followed central principles, with population size as the ratio. The population statistics were based on the household registration statistics compiled by the Ministry of Interior at the end of the 24th year and referred to the statistics reported to the Ministry this year. The minimum number of representatives for each province was nine, and the maximum was forty-four. The minimum number for each city was two, and the maximum was eight, to ensure that the quotas for each province and city did not differ too much, to prevent manipulation by provinces with larger populations, and to allow provinces and cities with smaller populations to jointly express their opinions on saving and building the country. The division of electoral districts in each province was based on the electoral district division table drafted by the Ministry of Interior, and the allocation of quotas for each electoral district was determined by the number of counties, cities, or administrative bureaus under its jurisdiction, in accordance with the spirit of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Founding Program, with each county electing one representative to participate in the legacy. The allocation of representative quotas for professional organizations was based on the reference materials from the Ministry of Industry for the survey of professional organizations in various provinces and cities, and the quotas allocated during the National Assembly were compared for appropriate allocation. The allocation of representative quotas for free professional organizations was also based on the reference materials provided by the Ministries of Interior, Industry, and Education. In the special elections, the allocation of representative quotas for the Northeastern provinces was handled according to central principles, and the Northeastern representative quotas were combined and distributed within the regional election quotas of various provinces and cities. Because their election methods were different, they were listed in the chapter on special elections. The allocation of representative quotas for Mongolia and Tibet adopted the opinions of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, with separate election procedures for those residing in and outside the region. The allocation of representative quotas for overseas Chinese adopted the opinions of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and compared the regulations of the National Assembly Representative Election Law. The allocation of representative quotas for the military adopted central principles, and the election methods adopted the opinions of the Military Affairs Commission. All of the above allocations were carefully studied and can be said to be fair and appropriate. At the beginning of the meeting on the 2nd, the second reading was held. Article 1 was changed to Article 2, paragraph 2, due to the change in the National Assembly Organization Law. Lu Zhiyi proposed an amendment to Article 5, which was not approved. In Article 35, Fu Bingchang proposed that the election of overseas Chinese should consider the revolutionary history in addition to the population ratio, because the revolutionary history of China can be said to be related to overseas Chinese on every page, and that the overseas Chinese in the United States and the Philippines should be given priority. He advocated adding one seat each to the United States and the Philippines and subtracting one seat each from Malaya and Siam, which was unanimously passed. Zhou Wei and Yang Gongda stated that the article referred to overseas Chinese as representatives from foreign countries and treated Hong Kong and Macau as foreign countries, which would imply a loss of national sovereignty. They proposed an amendment, and Huang Youchang proposed changing "foreign countries" to "overseas," which was passed without objection. Hang Jintao requested to increase the number of Mongolian representatives, which was not passed. Wu Huanzhang expressed disagreement with the article on representatives from the Northeastern provinces, which was listed as a special election. The chairman replied that this was because the election methods were different and did not mean that the Northeastern provinces were regarded as special regions. Subsequently, some committee members proposed changing the chapter on special elections to "Other Elections," "Mixed Elections," or "Special Elections," and others proposed deleting the chapter on special elections and listing the various elections for the Northeastern provinces, Mongolia and Tibet, overseas Chinese, and the military as separate chapters. Because Li Zhonggong, Zheng Hongnian, and others strongly advocated maintaining the original draft, no amendments were made. Articles 35 to 62 were passed according to the original draft. Then, with unanimous agreement, the third reading procedure was omitted and passed. The meeting adjourned at around 12:00 noon. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 2nd)

Total Number of Representatives: 1,200

(Nanjing) The National Assembly Representative Election Law passed by the Legislative Yuan on the 2nd has eight chapters: General Principles, Regional Elections, Occupational Elections, Special Elections (divided into four sections: Elections in the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe; Elections in Mongolia and Tibet; Elections for Overseas Chinese; and Elections for the Military), Election Headquarters and Election Supervision, Election and Invalid Election, Election Litigation, and Supplementary Provisions. The full text has 62 articles. The total number of National Assembly representatives is 1,200, with 665 elected by regional election methods, 380 elected by occupational election methods, and 155 elected by special election methods. The Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe representatives in the special elections do not distinguish between regional and occupational categories. The number of representatives is calculated as 14 for Liaoning, 13 for Jilin (two of which should be elected from the Eastern Province Special District), 9 for Heilongjiang, and 9 for Rehe. There are 24 representatives for Mongolia, 16 representatives for Tibet, and a total of 40 representatives for overseas Chinese, including one each in Honolulu, Peru, Mexico, Chile, Cuba, Central America, India, Europe, Korea, Tahiti, Macau, Japan, Australia, Africa, Hong Kong, and Taiwan, two each in Canada, the Philippines, and Burma, three each in the United Kingdom and Annam, and four each in Malaya, Siam, and the Dutch East Indies. There are 30 military representatives. Separate regulations govern the methods for the army, navy, and air force to nominate candidates. All other matters related to the election are stipulated in accordance with central principles. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 2nd)

The full text of the National Assembly Representative Election Law can be found on page 4.

Central Government Sends Personnel to Inspect the Dongzhuang Dam; Fu Rulin and Others Inspect the Jiangsu Dam and Closure Point; After Completion, the Project is Handed Over to Shandong's Receiving Personnel 5

(Jinan) This afternoon, Kong Xiangrong, accompanied by Fu Rulin, Shen Li, Wang Pingzheng, and other members of the Central Government's Dongzhuang Project Inspection Committee, as well as representatives from Shandong and Henan, inspected the Jiangsu Dam, the closure point, and the Fourth Diversion Canal at Dongzhuang. The committee members were very satisfied with the solidity of the project. After holding a closure banquet, the committee members returned to Kaifeng early on the 3rd and then returned to Nanjing to report. Kong and Pan Yifen, the representative from Shandong, are negotiating the handover procedures. (Special dispatch on the 2nd)

Li Shengcun: The ceremony for the closure and inspection of the Dongzhuang Yellow River breach closure project in Shandong was held in Dongzhuang on the 2nd. Various parties and the public sent commemorative items, which were dazzling. Kong Xiangrong, accompanied by Fu Rulin of the Inspection Committee of the Executive Yuan, Shen Li of the National Government, Wang Pingzheng of the Control Yuan, Yang Baopu and Tan Shengju, technical experts of the Executive Yuan, Wang Lutai, secretary of the Shandong Construction Department, Song Wentian, technical expert, Ma Yi, president of the Jinan branch of the Central Bank, Song Tong, representative of the Henan Provincial Government, Liu Zhuquan, representative of the Henan-Anhui Pacification Headquarters, Xie Zhian, representative of the Construction Department, Liu Butong, representative of the Party Department, and Wang Yujun, Zhu Yong, and Cai Zhen of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, left Kaifeng for Dongzhuang at 7:30 AM on the 2nd. They stopped at Liuzhuang Zhukou midway to inspect the dangerous works. Kong said that he planned to modify the Zhukou scouring dam into a stone dam. They arrived at Dongzhuang at noon. High pine squares were erected on the dam, and several cloth plaques were hung horizontally, reading "Welcome the Central Government Inspection and Supervision Officials." Pan Yifen, representative of the Provincial Government, also rushed from Jinan to participate in the ceremony and negotiate the takeover of the river defense. After Yu and others got off the car, they went to the breach closure project office to rest. The inspection ceremony was held at 2:00 PM, and the inspection procedures were carried out. Fu and others are scheduled to leave Dongzhuang and return to Nanjing on the 3rd. (Special dispatch on the 2nd)

Li Shengcun: At 2:30 PM on the 2nd, Fu, Shen, Wang, and other three senior officials, accompanied by Kong Xiangrong, inspected the closure project. Kong explained everything along the way. They first went to the Jiangsu Dam for inspection, then to the closure point for inspection. All the projects were extremely solid, and Fu and others expressed their deep admiration. The land outside the opening has dried up to form a water basin, occupying about 7 hectares, with many fish inside. Kong said that he planned to plant trees around it and place lotus flowers in the middle as a memorial. They then arrived at the Great King Temple to pay their respects and set off firecrackers, and then went to the Fourth Diversion Canal for inspection. Then they returned to the closure point for photography for commemoration. The construction site and office were plastered with slogans welcoming the Central Government Inspection Officials and Shandong Province Handover Committee. Soldiers from the Han Department's Pistol Brigade guarded everything, and there were several places performing plays to celebrate. A banquet was held in the office in the evening. The inspection officials are scheduled to leave Dongzhuang on the 3rd. The Yellow River post-disaster projects at breaches 1 to 5 have been repaired, and the sixth opening will also be completed soon. All the closure and completed projects will be handed over to Pan Yifen, the Shandong Provincial Government's handover commissioner, for handling. The post-disaster projects will be assisted by the Yellow River Conservancy Commission and the Shandong River Affairs Bureau. All materials and construction funds, except for a portion allocated for flood control, will be used for the embankment restoration project. At this point, the inspection and handover of the closure project have come to an end. The embankment restoration project is a separate phase, but it has already begun.

Li Shengcun: At 6:00 PM on the 2nd, Kong Xiangrong, accompanied by the three inspectors Fu, Wang, and Shen, and Zhang Huafu, Secretary-General of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, went to inspect Linpu Village, the hardest-hit area of the breach, which has now been restored. The area was originally the only prosperous commercial center in western Shandong for the concentration and transportation of local products. Now it is a desolate scene. The land is one or two zhang or even several zhang higher than before. Single-story houses only show the rooftops, and multi-story buildings have become single-story houses. Only the top of the gate of the Fourth Primary School of Juancheng County remains, and only the top of the door and the top of the stele of the Meng Temple remain. They returned at 3:00 AM and reported to the Central Government on the inspection of the closure project. (Special dispatch on the 1st)

Legislative Yuan Passes the National Assembly Representative Election Law: Full Text with 62 Articles and 4 Attached Tables 10

(Nanjing) The National Assembly Representative Election Law and four accompanying tables passed by the Legislative Yuan's general meeting on the 2nd are as follows:

Chapter 1: General Principles

Article 1: This law is formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 2, paragraph 2 of the National Assembly Organization Law.

Article 2: The total number of National Assembly representatives shall be 1,200, allocated according to the following clauses:

1. Those elected by regional election methods: 665 representatives.

2. Those elected by occupational election methods: 380 representatives.

3. Those elected by special election methods: 155 representatives.

Article 3: Citizens of the Republic of China who are 20 years of age or older and have taken a public oath have the right to elect National Assembly representatives.

Article 4: Anyone with one of the following circumstances shall not have the right to vote: Betraying the National Government, with a confirmed judgment or still wanted; Having committed corrupt acts while serving in public office, with a confirmed judgment or still wanted; Deprived of civil rights; Declared incompetent; Suffering from mental illness; Addicted to opium or its substitutes.

Article 5: Each elector may not have more than two voting rights.

Those who have voting rights in both regional and occupational elections shall participate in occupational elections.

Those who have voting rights in both special and occupational elections shall participate in special elections.

Those who have more than two voting rights in occupational elections may choose to be an elector of one group.

Article 6: The election of National Assembly representatives shall be conducted by unsigned, single-ballot method. The ballot shall contain the full names of all candidates designated by the National Government, and the elector shall circle one person from among them.

Article 7: The candidate with the most votes as described in the preceding article shall be elected as a National Assembly representative. If the number of votes is the same, a lottery shall be used to determine who is elected.

Article 8: After the legal number of National Assembly representatives has been elected in accordance with the provisions of the preceding article, the other candidates with votes shall be ranked in order of the number of votes as alternate National Assembly representatives. The number of alternates shall be the same as the number of those elected.

Chapter 2: Regional Elections

Article 9: The number of National Assembly representatives to be elected by each province and municipality directly under the Executive Yuan using regional election methods shall be as stipulated in Annex 1.

Article 10: National Assembly representatives from each province shall be elected by district. The division of electoral districts and the number of representatives to be elected from each district shall be as stipulated in Annex 2.

Article 11: Each electoral district shall jointly nominate candidates by the township heads and town heads of each county within the district. The number of candidates shall be ten times the number of National Assembly representatives to be elected from the district. If there is a city within the electoral district, the neighborhood chiefs shall participate in the nomination.

In counties and cities or administrative bureaus without township heads, town heads, or neighborhood chiefs, their equivalents shall participate in the nomination.

Article 12: Candidates in each electoral district shall possess the following qualifications: Possess the qualifications of an elector, but the oath of citizenship need not be taken within that electoral district; Be 25 years of age or older; Currently be a resident of that electoral district.

Article 13: The National Government shall designate three times the number of representatives to be elected from each electoral district from among the candidates nominated by each electoral district as candidates.

Article 14: The provincial government may make comments on the candidates nominated by each electoral district before submitting them to the National Government for designation.

Article 15: National Assembly representatives to be elected from each electoral district shall be elected by those with voting rights in each district in accordance with the provisions of Article 6.

Article 16: The nomination and designation of candidates for National Assembly representatives from municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan, and the election of representatives, shall be governed by the provisions of Articles 11 to 13 and 15.

Chapter 3: Occupational Elections

Article 17: The number of National Assembly representatives to be elected from various occupational groups in each province and municipality directly under the Executive Yuan shall be as stipulated in Annex 3.

Article 18: The election of National Assembly representatives from free professional groups shall not be divided by region, and the number of representatives shall be as stipulated in Annex 4.

Article 19: The occupational groups and free professional groups participating in the election shall be limited to those established in accordance with the law before the promulgation of this law.

Article 20: Occupational groups in each province shall nominate candidates by the officials of the organizations of each group. The number of candidates shall be three times the number of representatives to be elected from each group.

The officials of the organizations mentioned in the preceding paragraph shall be limited to the officials of the executive organs of each occupational group.

Article 21: Candidates from occupational groups in each province shall possess the following qualifications: Possess the qualifications of an elector; Be 25 years of age or older; Have been engaged in the respective occupation for more than three years; Currently be a member of the respective group. If the years of engaging in the occupation mentioned in the preceding paragraph are interrupted, the periods shall be calculated by combining them.

Article 22: The National Government shall designate twice the number of representatives to be elected from each group from among the candidates nominated by occupational groups in each province as candidates.

Article 23: National Assembly representatives to be elected from occupational groups in each province shall be elected by members of each occupational group who have the right to vote under this law in accordance with the provisions of Article 6.

Article 24: If the organization of an occupational group in each province has several levels, the nomination of candidates for National Assembly representatives shall be carried out by the officials of the lowest-level organization of each occupational group. The election of National Assembly representatives shall be carried out by the members of the lowest-level organization of each occupational group. If a member of an occupational group is an organization, the election of National Assembly representatives shall be carried out by the members of the member organization.

Article 25: The nomination and designation of candidates for National Assembly representatives from various occupational groups in municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan, and the election of representatives, shall be governed by the provisions of Articles 20 to 24.

Article 26: The nomination and designation of candidates for National Assembly representatives from free professional groups, and the election of representatives, shall be governed by the provisions regarding occupational groups.

Chapter 4: Special Elections

Section 1: Elections in the Four Provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe

Article 27: The election of National Assembly representatives from Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe shall not be divided by region or occupation. The number of representatives shall be as follows:

Liaoning Province: 14 representatives.

Jilin Province: 13 representatives.

Heilongjiang Province: 9 representatives.

Rehe Province: 9 representatives.

Within the number of representatives from Jilin Province mentioned in the preceding paragraph, two representatives shall be elected from the Eastern Province Special Region.

Article 28: Candidates for National Assembly representatives from Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe shall be designated by the National Government. The number of candidates shall be three times the number of representatives to be elected from each province.

Article 29: For the election of National Assembly representatives from Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe, the election headquarters shall issue election certificates. Those with voting rights in each province shall collect them from the election supervisor in the province or region where they are located.

Article 30: After obtaining the election certificate, electors may vote in accordance with the provisions of Article 6 at the venue designated by the election supervisor mentioned in the preceding article, or mail the ballot directly to the chief election supervisor. The aforementioned ballots shall be separately prepared and delivered to the chief election supervisor for counting.

Section 2: Elections in Mongolia and Tibet

Article 31: The number of National Assembly representatives to be elected from Mongolia shall be as follows:

1. Those elected from the Xilingol League, Ulanqab League, Ikhezhao League, Qinghai Left Wing League, Qinghai Right Wing League, Chahar Department, Alxa Special Banner, Ejin Special Banner, and Shumeite Special Banner: 9 representatives.

2. Those elected from the Batu Setkhiltur League, the Middle Route League of the Urad Front Banner, and the Qingsetkhiltu League: 3 representatives.

3. Those elected from the Jirim League, Josutu League, Joo-Uda League, Hulunbuir Department, and Ikhe Minggan Special Banner: 5 representatives.

4. Those elected from various old leagues and banners: 7 representatives.

Article 32: The number of National Assembly representatives to be elected from Tibet shall be as follows:

1. Those elected by those with voting rights in the Tibetan region: 10 representatives.

2. Those elected by Tibetan people with voting rights in other provinces and regions: 6 representatives.

Article 33: The nomination and designation of candidates for National Assembly representatives to be elected as stipulated in Article 31, paragraph 1, paragraph 2, and Article 32, paragraph 1, and the election of representatives, shall be governed by the provisions regarding regional elections in each province, respectively.

Article 34: The nomination and designation of candidates for National Assembly representatives to be elected as stipulated in Article 31, paragraph 3, paragraph 4, and Article 32, paragraph 2, and the election of representatives, shall be governed by the provisions regarding the elections in the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe, respectively.

Section 3: Elections of Overseas Chinese

Article 35: The number of National Assembly representatives to be elected by overseas Chinese shall be as follows:

One representative in Honolulu, one in Chile,

One in Peru, one in Cuba,

One in Mexico, one in Central America,

Three in the United States, two in the Philippines,

Two in Canada, four in Malaya,

One in India, two in Burma,

Three in Annam, four in Siam,

One in Europe, one in Japan,

One in Korea, one in Australia,

One in Tahiti, one in Africa,

Four in the Dutch territories, one in Hong Kong,

One in Macau, one in Taiwan.

Article 36: The nomination and designation of candidates for National Assembly representatives to be elected by overseas Chinese shall be governed by the provisions regarding occupational elections. However, the groups nominating candidates shall be determined by the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission.

Article 37: The election of National Assembly representatives to be elected by overseas Chinese shall be governed by the provisions regarding regional elections in each province.

Section 4: Elections in the Military

Article 38: The national army, navy, air force, and military education institutions shall elect 30 National Assembly representatives.

Article 39: Candidates for National Assembly representatives from the military shall be nominated in accordance with the following methods: Each army division shall nominate two candidates. Each independent brigade or special force with more than two regiments shall nominate one candidate. Independent units with less than two regiments shall jointly nominate candidates with the divisions, independent brigades, or special forces stationed nearby. The navy shall nominate one candidate from each fleet directly under the Ministry of the Navy. The Marine Corps shall jointly nominate one candidate. Other units shall be designated by the Ministry of the Navy and jointly nominate candidates with fleets or the Marine Corps directly under the Ministry of the Navy. The Air Force shall jointly nominate one candidate. Military education institutions shall jointly nominate two candidates. The National Government shall designate 90 candidates from among the candidates nominated in the preceding paragraph as candidates.

Article 40: National Assembly representatives from the military shall be elected by officers and soldiers of the army, navy, air force, and military education institutions who have the right to vote under this law from among the candidates designated by the National Government in accordance with the provisions of Article 6.

Article 41: Candidates for National Assembly representatives from the military shall possess the following qualifications: Possess the qualifications of an elector; Be 25 years of age or older; Have served in the National Revolutionary Army for more than five years and have made outstanding achievements, or have graduated from a military education institution and have excellent academic performance.

Chapter 5: Election Headquarters and Election Supervisors

Article 42: The central government shall establish a National Assembly Representative Election Headquarters, directly under the National Government, with one director and one deputy director, specially appointed to direct and supervise the national election affairs. The organization of the Election Headquarters shall be determined by order.

Article 43: Each province shall establish a chief election supervisor, to be concurrently held by the head of the Department of Civil Affairs.

Each electoral district within the province shall establish an election supervisor, to be concurrently held by the highest administrative head of the district. In the absence of a highest administrative head, the Election Headquarters shall appoint one from among the administrative heads within the district.

Article 44: Municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan shall establish an election supervisor, to be concurrently held by the mayor.

Article 45: For the elections in the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe, and free professional groups, the Minister of the Interior shall be the chief election supervisor.

For the elections in Mongolia and Tibet, the Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission shall be the chief election supervisor.

For the elections of overseas Chinese, the Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission shall be the chief election supervisor.

For the elections in the military, the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission shall be the chief election supervisor.

Article 46: Election supervisors may be established for the elections in Mongolia, Tibet, overseas Chinese, and the military, to be appointed by the Election Headquarters.

Article 47: The qualifications of nominators, electors, and candidates shall be reviewed by the election supervisor.

Article 48: The election date and election venues shall be determined by the election supervisor.

Article 49: For voting and ballot counting related to the election of National Assembly representatives, polling station administrators, polling station inspectors, ballot counting administrators, and ballot counting inspectors shall be appointed by the election supervisor.

Article 50: Election supervisors and the officials mentioned in the preceding article shall not be candidates for National Assembly representatives in the region or group where they are conducting the election.

Article 51: The certificate of election for National Assembly representatives shall be issued by the election supervisor.

Chapter 6: Invalid Election and Election

Article 52: The election shall be invalid in any of the following circumstances: The register of electors involves fraud that affects one-third or more of the electors in the register, as determined by a confirmed judgment; The conduct of the election violates laws and regulations, as determined by a confirmed judgment.

Article 52: If an election is invalid, a new election shall be held immediately in accordance with the law.

However, this shall not apply in special circumstances where a new election cannot be held in time.

Article 54: The election shall be invalid in any of the following circumstances: Death; The candidate does not meet the qualifications, as determined by a confirmed judgment; The number of votes obtained is false, as determined by a confirmed judgment.

Article 55: If the election is invalid, or if the elected person is unwilling to serve, the alternate candidate stipulated in Article 8 shall be successively appointed.

Chapter 7: Election Lawsuits

Article 56: If an elector or losing candidate confirms that the election officials have committed fraud or other violations of laws and regulations, they may file a lawsuit within ten days from the date of the election.

Article 57: If an elector or losing candidate confirms that the elected person does not meet the qualifications, or that the number of votes is false, or if a losing candidate confirms that the number of votes they obtained should have resulted in election but did not, they may file a lawsuit within five days from the date of the announcement of the names of the elected persons.

Article 58: Election lawsuits shall be under the jurisdiction of the competent High Court and shall be given priority over other lawsuits for trial. The first instance shall be final.

Lawsuits concerning military elections shall be tried by the Military Law Department of the Military Affairs Commission.

Article 59: Crimes concerning elections shall be punished in accordance with the Criminal Law.

Chapter 8: Supplementary Provisions

Article 60: The power to interpret this law belongs to the National Assembly Representative Election Headquarters.

Article 61: The detailed rules for the implementation of this law shall be determined by order.

Article 62: The date of implementation of this law shall be determined by order. Annex 1: Table of the Number of National Assembly Representatives to be Elected by Each Province and Municipality Directly under the Executive Yuan Using Regional Election Methods.

Jiangsu: 44 representatives, Zhejiang: 33 representatives, Anhui: 35 representatives, Jiangxi: 28 representatives, Hubei: 40 representatives, Hunan: 43 representatives, Sichuan: 44 representatives, Xikang: 9 representatives, Hebei: 43 representatives, Shandong: 44 representatives (one of which shall be elected from the Weihaiwei Administrative Region), Shanxi: 22 representatives, Henan: 44 representatives, Shaanxi: 20 representatives, Gansu: 14 representatives, Qinghai: 9 representatives, Fujian: 22 representatives, Guangdong: 44 representatives, Guangxi: 21 representatives, Yunnan: 22 representatives, Guizhou: 16 representatives, Chahar: 10 representatives, Suiyuan: 10 representatives, Ningxia: 9 representatives, Xinjiang: 12 representatives, Nanjing: 4 representatives, Shanghai: 8 representatives, Beiping: 6 representatives, Tianjin: 5 representatives, Qingdao: 2 representatives, Xijing: 2 representatives (Total: 665 representatives)

Annex 2: Table of the Division of Electoral Districts in Each Province and the Number of National Assembly Representatives to be Elected from Each District (Omitted)

Annex 3: Table of the Number of National Assembly Representatives to be Elected from Various Occupational Groups in Each Province and Municipality Directly under the Executive Yuan.

Su: Farmers' Association: 7, Labor Union: 7, Chamber of Commerce: 7, Total: 21.

Zhe: Farmers' Association: 5, Labor Union: 5, Chamber of Commerce: 5, Total: 15.
