We are delighted to hear this good news. From now on, the foundation will be solid, laying the foundation for the party and the nation. The great cause will be brilliant, breaking the established rules of ancient times. We hereby send our congratulations and hope for your understanding." It is also reported that Mr. Rui Qingrong, owner of the Xinguang Grand Theater, who has always had patriotic enthusiasm, specially requested Shi Chunxuan, Wang Xiaoxin, Xiao Wenbin, Liu Ziyun, and all the male and female stars to perform Shanghai opera for one day, donating all the proceeds to the aircraft purchase fund. It is reported that the ticket sales totaled 330.20 yuan in national currency, which is a great achievement.

Yesterday's Resolution by the Foreign Tea Merchants' Association: Accepting Advice to Resume Cashing Checks; Specific Measures to be Decided at Today's Emergency Meeting; Foreign Merchants in Shanghai Urgently Request Sample Shipments for Trading; Yesterday Evening's Reception to Various Circles to Report on the Progress 64

According to the New Voice Society, regarding the Foreign Tea Merchants' Association, after Anhui Province controlled Qihong tea and suspended check cashing, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter advising them not to persist in their obstinacy and to resume cashing checks immediately in order to maintain the livelihood of tea farmers and merchants. The association held a meeting yesterday and expressed its acceptance in principle. However, specific measures must await further emergency meeting at 2:00 PM today to discuss and decide. The association hosted a reception for various circles last night to report on the progress. Details are recorded as follows:

Jingdezhen Requests Order to Cash Checks

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a letter yesterday from the Jingdezhen Money Exchange Association, which stated: "We are writing to inform you that, according to reports from various firms in our association, tea firms have purchased drafts from various Shanghai tea warehouses to be cashed in Shanghai. These drafts, worth over 100,000 yuan, are now being held for ten days. We have received a telegram from Shanghai stating that all drafts from tea warehouses, regardless of origin, have been suspended, and many drafts that have already been signed and due have been returned. Our industry has been hit hard and is in a state of panic. We have investigated and found that drafts issued by tea warehouses have always been highly reliable, and in past incidents, they have always been cashed. Therefore, our firms have welcomed and accepted them. Now, the sudden suspension of cashing not only makes it difficult for firms to operate, but also creates an emergency in the financial market. At a time of economic exhaustion, we cannot withstand this unexpected blow. We have decided in a full meeting that, in addition to requesting the Jingdezhen Chamber of Commerce to telegraph your association to allow the maintenance of credit, we are specially writing to request you to forward this request to the Tea Merchants' Association to order the tea warehouses to cash the drafts according to the bills in order to maintain credit and stabilize commerce. We await your urgent instructions."

Foreign Firms Request Immediate Sample Shipments for Trading

A letter from Duder Foreign Firm in Shanghai stated: "We are writing to inform you that we have heard that red and green teas from various regions are arriving, and some have already arrived. However, we have not seen any samples sent by the warehouses. We hope you will immediately notify the warehouses to send samples to our firm as soon as possible. Respectfully, to the Foreign Tea Merchants' Association." A letter from the China Tea Company stated: "We are writing to inform you that we have heard that your members have not yet sent out samples. We are not sure why. Last year at this time, new green teas from Huzhou and other places were already on the market for trade. Now, there is silence. Foreign countries are eagerly requesting new goods, and telegrams and letters are urging. The shipment and sale of domestic products should not be delayed. We are writing to request that you inform your member warehouses to send samples for negotiation as soon as possible. Do not delay. Respectfully, to the Foreign Tea Merchants' Association." A letter from the Fushi Foreign Firm in Shanghai stated: "We are writing to inform you that our firm's transactions always abide by the association's regulations. We have recently heard that red and green teas have arrived, but we have not seen samples displayed. Please ask the warehouses to send samples to our firm immediately for trading. Please do not delay. Respectfully, to the Tea Merchants' Association."

The Chamber of Commerce Advises Against Stubbornness

"We are writing to inform you that your association previously decided to suspend all outstanding drafts due to the seizure of Qihong tea operations by Anhui Province's control. Our association believes that this matter is related to the tea market and involves finance, so we requested a serious consideration. You kindly postponed it for two days, but ultimately, as the deadline approached, you did not receive a reply from the Anhui Provincial Government and were forced to implement it, which is deeply regrettable. Since then, the Zhide County Chamber of Commerce, the Jingdezhen Money Exchange Association, and others have telegraphed our association, stating that these drafts are essential for the financial turnover in those areas. Once suspended, it would cause financial panic and have a huge impact. They requested that our association advise your association to cash the drafts. We have forwarded these letters to you from time to time, but we have not received a reply. Your association certainly has its own difficulties, but this case is centered on the Red Tea Transportation and Sales Committee, not the tea firms that are being controlled. If you say that the tea firms are persuading the Anhui Provincial Government to change its policy by suspending the checks, then the tea firms and tea warehouses have had decades of friendship. If they can help, they would be happy to do so. We fear that the current situation is similar to your industry. Therefore, our intention is to strive to preserve your business as one thing, and to safeguard the credit of the drafts as another. We believe that you are targeting the wrong object, which is similar to what the ancients called 'venting anger on the wrong person,' and may even lose the sympathy of the domestic tea industry, and even give an excuse to those who advocate large-scale control. Our association shares your concerns, and we dare not fail to offer our loyal and well-intentioned advice. We have also heard that the Anhui Provincial Government has sent personnel to Shanghai to discuss solutions with your industry for the Qihong tea business. We urge you not to miss the opportunity, to immediately resume cashing checks to maintain the inherent credit of the tea industry for decades, and to send personnel to negotiate in order to achieve a turnaround. Do not persist in your obstinacy. Moreover, the point of contention for your industry lies in Qihong tea, but the scope of the suspension extends to green tea. Now, various types of green tea are about to enter the market, and there is an urgent need for funds. It is even more appropriate to resume cashing checks immediately to maintain the livelihood of tea farmers and merchants. As soon as new teas from various regions arrive, you should immediately send samples to avoid missing the market situation. This matter concerns the people's livelihood and the national economy. We hope you will adopt our advice. Respectfully, to the Shanghai Foreign Tea Merchants' Association."

The Association Resolves to Accept the Principle

The Foreign Tea Merchants' Association held an emergency meeting at the association at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Representatives from fourteen firms, including Zhongxinpu, Zhenhe Deng Yongxiang, Yitai Fan Baosheng, Yuanfengrun Zheng Jianyuan, Gongshengyong Peng Zhiping, Shenyuan Sun Zifu, Rendenyong Ye Yonghui, Shengchangsheng Zai Yintao, Yilong Deng Ruixian, Xietai Ye Shichang, Tongtai Tao Zhensheng, and Xielong Shan Jianming, were present. Chairman Chen Yizhou reported on the letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce advising them to resume cashing checks as usual and the letters from various foreign firms urging them to send new tea samples for trading. After a long discussion, it was resolved to accept the principle of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's advice. However, specific measures must await another emergency meeting at 2:00 PM this afternoon to discuss and decide. Furthermore, the cashing of term bills for green tea is easier to resolve, while the problem of red tea is that the funds and tea are not in place, so other solutions should be sought. At 3:00 PM, all attending representatives, led by Chen Yizhou, went to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to discuss solutions.

Seeking Solutions by Visiting the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Upon receiving the reply from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce advising them to resume cashing checks and resume business, the Foreign Tea Merchants' Association, led by Chen Yizhou, Hong Mengpan, Sun Zifu, and other seventeen representatives, went to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to discuss. Secretary Yan Esheng received them and immediately announced that the association was advising the tea industry to resume cashing checks and resume business because green tea was about to enter the market and the opportunity could not be missed. Moreover, the suspension of cashing had lasted for nearly ten days, and the financial situation in various regions was being affected. If this continued, it would inevitably cause the national economy and the people's livelihood to suffer. He hoped that the tea industry would accept the advice of the Chamber of Commerce and resume cashing checks immediately. At the same time, the Chamber of Commerce would continue to telegraph the government to maintain the situation in order to achieve the goal of balancing considerations. The representatives of the tea industry expressed their willingness to accept the Chamber of Commerce's good intentions and to resume cashing checks for the green tea portion as usual. However, for the Qihong tea portion, the funds and tea were not in place, so other solutions should be determined. Yan immediately stated that the tea industry could decide on detailed measures and then report them to the Chamber of Commerce for review.

Hosting a Reception to Report on the Progress

The Foreign Tea Merchants' Association hosted a reception at the New New Restaurant at 7:00 PM yesterday, inviting all executive and supervisory committee members of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, including Yu Zuoting, as well as Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Guo Shun, and over a hundred journalists from various newspapers. Chen Yizhou reported that "Tonight, we have prepared a simple feast and respectfully invited the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the press, various public organizations, and Mr. Yu Qiaqing. We are very honored. On behalf of our association's Chairman Hong, I would like to offer a few humble words and sincerely thank you for your kind intentions. In April 1st, the Anhui Provincial Government suddenly established the Qimen Red Tea Transportation and Sales Committee. The main idea was to revive Qihong tea in name, but in reality, it was to seize the business of the tea warehouses. Our association first requested the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to telegraph the Economic Committee and received a reply stating that the business of the tea warehouses had been taken into consideration and that there was no control over Qihong tea. We telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Government and received a reply stating that there was no control over Qihong tea, that it would not hinder the tea warehouses from lending money, and that there was no need to worry. Therefore, the tea warehouses proceeded to issue over one million yuan in drafts. Because the Anhui Provincial Transportation and Sales Committee was established, in addition to requesting the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward telegrams to higher levels and Anhui Province, we also sent three representatives to Anhui to petition. As a result, transportation was to be done by the government and sales by merchants. We formally submitted a petition, added further entreaties, and appointed He Jefu and others to go to Qi to implement the lending of money to various tea firms. The tea firms unanimously refused, stating that they had already received funds from the tea warehouses and would no longer receive government funds. After persisting for many days, He Jefu and others first used sweet words to induce them, and then used official authority to force the tea firms to receive government funds even though they had already received warehouse funds, and transportation and sales were to be done by the government. Now, they have completely seized the business. The tea firms that had already received drafts from the tea warehouses were induced to have Qi Fu telegraph the Ministry of Industry to welcome the Transportation and Sales Office's lending of money. He Jefu and others, relying on loans from the bank and official power, took over the business of the tea warehouses that had been around for seventy or eighty years. Later, they falsely accused the tea warehouses of using the suspension of cashing as a threat. It is like killing someone and not allowing them to cry out. The cruel deprivation is unscrupulous. We speculate that their intention is to use transportation and sales as a banner. If there is a road and enough vehicles can be prepared, the tea firms would certainly be happy to comply. Why force them to register for official transportation, and not allow transportation without official permission? As for the word 'sales,' how will they sell it? There is no master plan. It is just empty talk for momentary gratification. They declare that Shanghai is the main sales office and London is the branch sales office. The decline of Chinese tea is entirely blamed on the tea warehouses. They have even forgotten the fundamental word 'fundamental.' What is fundamental? It is improving production. Have the proponents ever considered this? It is as if hanging a transportation and sales sign will transfer the tea market and reap all the benefits. Because the commander's price is appropriate, the tea price will inevitably increase, so they disregard everything and seize the opportunity. They falsely accuse the tea warehouses of exploitation in order to satisfy their insatiable desires. The tea warehouses keep accounts, and every entry has a basis. Except for the use of gold, everything else is the amount paid on behalf of others. Gentlemen, uphold justice, send letters and telegrams, and appeal on our behalf. Some take on the role of Lu Lian, while others offer public commentary. The spirit of the late Premier in heaven upholds freedom of business, and there will eventually be a day when justice is served. We hope you will frequently provide guidance, offer advice, and vigorously support us. Conscience is a great help. We and our colleagues will stand up and offer a toast to the health of all of you." The reception ended around 9:00 PM.

Unifying Red Tea Transportation and Sales: Objectives: Reducing Costs; Developing Trade; Balancing Production and Sales; Rescuing Rural Areas 65

According to the Central News Agency, since the governments of Anhui and Jiangxi provinces decided to unify the transportation and sales of red tea and organized the Anhui-Jiangxi Red Tea Transportation and Sales Committee, the Shanghai foreign tea warehouses have risen up to appeal, and letters and telegrams have been sent in succession, drawing worldwide attention. Minister Kong recently stated that the purpose of unifying the transportation and sales of red tea in the two provinces is to balance production and sales and improve quality. Merchants believe that the government is competing with the people for profit, which is a misunderstanding. However, the tea warehouses have not ceased their disputes due to Minister Kong's remarks. It has recently been heard that Qian Chengxu, representing the National Federation of Industries, has gone to Anhui to negotiate on behalf of the tea warehouses in order to protect their interests. What the truth is, the outside world is unsure. In order to understand the essence of this unified red tea transportation and sales event decided by the two provincial governments, the reporter went to the deputy manager of the Anhui-Jiangxi Red Tea Transportation and Sales Committee's General Transportation and Sales Office, Zeng Yucheng. Mr. Zeng, as a representative of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, personally participated in the measures taken by the two provincial governments. He agreed to inform us of the process by which the two provincial governments handled the unified transportation and sales of red tea, as follows:

Negotiation Process and Transportation and Sales Plan

Regarding the motives and process of the two provincial governments handling the unified transportation and sales of red tea, Mr. Zeng first stated that the gradual decline of red tea trade is an undeniable fact, and it is the government's natural responsibility to take urgent action to save it. In February of this year, the National Economic Commission convened a tea technology discussion meeting, and the Anhui Construction Department proposed unifying the transportation and sales of Qihong tea to facilitate international trade. The proposal was approved at the meeting. The Anhui Provincial Government, based on the principles approved by the meeting, sent personnel to Jiangxi to negotiate and expand the scope of unified transportation and sales. Zhao, Director of the Agricultural Department of the National Economic Commission, Xiao Chunjin, a member of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, and He Chongjie, a representative of the Anhui Provincial Government, actively planned and decided on the organization of the Anhui-Jiangxi Red Tea Transportation and Sales Committee and the outline of its business plan. The Anhui-Jiangxi Red Tea Transportation and Sales Committee was formally established in Anqing on April 1st, and Zhao Lianfang, Director of the National Economic Commission, and the directors of the financial and construction departments of Anhui and Jiangxi provinces were appointed as standing committee members. Various important cases were also discussed and decided. Regarding transportation and sales, the highway bureaus of the two provinces fully prepared vehicles to accept tea from merchants at the bus stations in the Qimen and Fuliang production areas, transport them to Xuancheng and Yingtan separately, and transfer them to the Jiangnan Railway and the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway to Shanghai. This would ensure safety and save time. The freight would be slightly lower than the previous method of transporting by Poyang Lake to Jiujiang and then loading onto ships. The Zhide tea boxes would also be loaded onto ships in Anqing, which would be very convenient. Regarding promotion, a general transportation and sales office would be set up in Shanghai, and Chinese and foreign tea masters would be hired to organize a tea quality assessment committee to balance market prices. Tea prices would not be suppressed, and foreign merchants would not be deceived. A branch sales office would also be set up in London to seek direct exports and contact Russia to restore the original market. Regarding loans, there were three items. The first item was that the Anhui Construction Department and the Bank of Communications jointly raised 400,000 yuan, with Anhui accounting for 20% and the Bank of Communications accounting for 80%, to be lent to the tea cooperatives in Qimen. The second item was that the Anhui and Jiangxi provincial governments and the Anhui Local Bank jointly raised 1.4 million yuan, with the local bank accounting for 80%, or 1.12 million yuan, and the remaining 20% being 200,000 yuan from Anhui and 80,000 yuan from Jiangxi. All of this was lent to the tea firms in Qimen, Zhide, and Fuliang counties at a monthly interest rate of 8%, not compound interest, and to be repaid by the end of the year. If the tea had not been sold by then, the deadline could be extended for two months. The third item was that the Tingxi Yumin Bank alone provided a loan of 300,000 yuan to Xiuwu, Tonggu, and Wuling counties, with the same interest rate as Anhui, which was also 8%.

Over One Hundred Tea Firms Registered

Mr. Zeng continued that the registration of tea firms in Qimen, Zhide, and Fuliang counties had been completed. A total of 125 tea firms were registered in Qimen, 76 in Fuliang, and over 40 in Zhide. The total amount of loans issued was over 1.5 million yuan, exceeding the planned amount by over 100,000 yuan. The total number of tea boxes in the three counties was estimated to be over 50,000 boxes, which should be suitable for the market's needs.

Four Steps to Rescue

Regarding the government's purpose of unifying the transportation and sales of red tea, Mr. Zeng solemnly declared that it was definitely not to seek financial income in the name of unified transportation and sales, nor to compete with the people for profit. The government was guaranteeing bank investment and contributing 20%. In the event of any losses to the bank in the future, the government's 20% would be used to cover them first. Therefore, the government was spending a large amount of money to handle unified transportation and sales. The government intends to take four steps to rescue red tea, namely (1) production, (2) manufacturing, (3) transportation, and (4) sales. The issues of production and manufacturing are matters of time. New planting and manufacturing methods are being tested and promoted by the tea improvement center. The issues of transportation and sales are economic and organizational issues. It is beneficial to the future of tea trade for the government to improve transportation and sales with its power. The decline of Chinese red tea in the world market is mainly due to high costs. Improving transportation and sales is aimed at addressing high costs. After unified transportation and sales, costs can definitely be reduced. (1) The interest rate on loans from tea warehouses used to be 1.5% per month. Now, the interest rate on government loans is 8% per month, reducing the interest rate by nearly half. (2) In the past, tea boxes from tea firms were transported through Poyang Lake to Jiujiang and then to Shanghai, which involved many risks. Last year, over 2,000 tea boxes sank in Poyang Lake, and the losses were too great for merchants to bear. Moreover, the freight from Poyang Lake to Jiujiang and then to Shanghai was quite expensive. Now, the government unifies transportation and sales, using a combination of highways and railways, which is both safe and fast, and the freight is also particularly cheap. (3) In the past, tea firms entrusted all sales of tea to tea warehouses, and commissions and other expenses accounted for nearly 15% of the tea's selling price. Now, the government only charges a 2% handling fee for unified transportation and sales, and nothing else. The government believes that after these three improvements, costs can be reduced, and lower costs and favorable exchange rates will make the future of red tea trade more optimistic. The government will take some time to actively work on production and manufacturing, and there is hope for reversing the crisis of red tea.

Regrettable Opposition from Tea Warehouses

Mr. Zeng expressed his regret for the opposition from the local tea warehouses. Mr. Zeng believed that the tea warehouses should not hinder the entire red tea business for the sake of a few private interests. Whether the tea warehouses themselves exist is a matter of time. As times advance, trade becomes more direct. Goods are sold directly from producers to consumers, which benefits both producers and consumers. The transfer of goods by intermediaries cannot be allowed to increase unless absolutely necessary. The more intermediaries there are, the more the cost increases. Reducing the transfer of goods by intermediaries is an indelible theory in economics. The tea warehouses do not understand this and oppose the government's measures in every way, disregarding the position of red tea in international trade, which seems to violate the spirit of the times. After the invention of the streetcar, rickshaw pullers were greatly panicked and suddenly destroyed the streetcars. In reality, the operation of the streetcars will not be stopped by the destruction of the rickshaws, and the work of rickshaw pullers will continue to be needed in other ways and will be able to survive at the same time. The opposition of the tea warehouses to the government's measures is no different from the rickshaw pullers' opposition to the streetcars and ignores that the unified transportation and sales measures are a product of the times. The position of the tea warehouses themselves is the same as that of rickshaw pullers and may not be completely eliminated after unified transportation and sales. Moreover, the government has fully considered the issue of the tea warehouses' debts and the issue of the tea warehouses' unemployment. There are three measures to consider the position of the tea warehouses: To recruit tea warehouse talent as much as possible to assist in the committee's affairs. For the old debts owed by tea merchants to tea warehouses, both parties will be convened after the tea is sold to handle them according to custom. If there are disputes, the two parties will resolve them according to law. For tea firms that have received funds from tea warehouses this year, if the tea warehouses do not want to provide further loans, the committee can review and transfer the loans and interest. For the tea warehouses' sake, they should support the government's measures and contribute their experience and manpower to the government, working together to seek the development of red tea trade. I personally believe that if the tea warehouse gentlemen change their attitude of opposing the government and cooperate with the government, the government will not hesitate to protect the interests of the tea warehouses themselves. If the tea warehouses continue to dispute, the government is bound by public orders and has already done its best to accommodate them.

Detailed Measures Implemented Step by Step

Mr. Zeng concluded that unified transportation and sales is the initial goal of rescuing red tea. The government will further plan detailed measures and implement them step by step to seek direct benefits for farmers in the two provinces. It is hoped that people from all walks of life will rise up to assist, and the improvement of the lives of farmers in the two provinces depends on this.

An Overview of the Investigation and Confiscation of Smuggled Goods in the North Station Area in the Past Week: A Total of Twenty-Two Cases of Undervalued Foreign Silk were Confiscated, with an Estimated Total Value of Over 30,000 Yuan 66

From April 27th to yesterday (May 2nd) of this month, every day, flat-Shanghai through passenger trains and freight trains arrived with undervalued foreign silk. Two cases were confiscated in Nanxiang, three cases were confiscated in Zhenru, and seventeen cases were confiscated in the North Station. The total value of the undervalued foreign silk was over 30,000 yuan. Yesterday, Mr. Balunsen, the customs commissioner of the customs service, specially sent customs officers to the North Station to load the 50 large bundles of stored undervalued foreign silk back to the customs for sale and confiscation. It is heard that the customs and the railway have established close ties, so the investigation and confiscation work will definitely be more properly carried out in the future.

Spring Cocoon Lending in the Financial Community: More Banks and Money Shops Joining: General Agreement on the Silver Group Organization 67

The Shanghai financial community has jointly formed a silver group to provide loans for the spring cocoon harvest of the 25th year. The fourteen initiating banks, including the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, held a meeting a few days ago and decided that the total amount of loans to be provided would be 30 million yuan, and that the interest rate, term, and procedures would be determined. In recent days, representatives from seven banks, including the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Shanghai Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Jiangsu Farmers Bank, the Jiangsu Bank, and the Four-Bank Savings Association, have been drafting the organizational charter and loan procedures. It is scheduled to convene a general meeting on the 10th to discuss and pass them, and then begin setting up an office and start providing loans. It is heard that the financial community in Shanghai generally agrees with the silver group organization, so three banks, including Xinhua, Quangong, and Zhizhong, participated a few days ago. Now, two more banks, Yongyong and Da, and the Fuyuan Money Shop, have requested to participate.

Zheng Chengqing's Pretext for Investigation: Municipal Chamber of Commerce Resolves Dismissal and Expulsion, Submitted for Approval at the June 20th General Meeting, Legal Matters to Be Prosecuted According to Law 68

According to Xin Sheng She, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce held its 18th Executive Committee meeting at 4:00 PM on the day before yesterday (the 1st). The attending executive committee members were Yu Zuoting, Ke Ganchen, Xu Jiliao, Pan Xusheng, Ma Jiliang, Ye Yinshan, Xu Guanqun, Ma Shaoquan, Zheng Zenan, and Jin Runxiang. The supervisory committee members present were Fang Jiaobo, Pei Yunqing, Chen Ziming, and Luo Qinghua. Chairman Yu Zuoting presided over the meeting, and after formalities, the discussion began on the case of Executive Committee member Zheng Chengqing falsely using the chairman's name to investigate the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Company. First, Secretary Yan Esheng read the report from the Standing Committee regarding the case, the letter from the Supervisory Committee, and the letter of resignation from Executive Committee member Zheng Chengqing due to illness. The attending committee members then expressed their opinions and, after detailed discussion, it was resolved that Executive Committee member Zheng Chengqing, due to improper conduct that harmed the reputation and credit of the Chamber of Commerce, should be subjected to dismissal and expulsion in accordance with Articles 17 and 22, Clause 3 of the Chamber of Commerce Law. This resolution will be submitted to the General Meeting of Members for approval. As for the legal aspects concerning Zheng Chengqing and Zhang Bofang, the Chamber of Commerce shall prosecute them according to law, and the representing lawyer shall be hired by the Standing Committee. Also, the date of the General Meeting of Members was discussed and it was resolved to hold it at 1:00 PM on June 20th. Membership applications will be suspended from May 21st to June 20th, and the period from May 11th to June 10th will be for collecting membership fees, re-electing representatives, and collecting proposals. The meeting adjourned. Attached are the two reports and letters regarding the Zheng case:

Standing Committee Report

On April 17th of this year, the Secretariat of the Chamber of Commerce received a notice from the Chairman, convening a temporary emergency meeting at 2:00 PM that afternoon. All members of the Standing Committee attended. After the meeting began, Chairman Yu reported that Executive Committee member Zheng Chengqing had allegedly borrowed the Chairman's name to pretextually investigate, etc., the Shanghai Textile Printing and Dyeing Company, and attached two pieces of evidence, requesting a thorough investigation. After discussion, it was resolved that if this matter were true, it should be handled strictly according to law. However, to be prudent, the Supervisory Committee was requested to thoroughly investigate the facts before further action. After the resolution, it was recorded and a letter was sent to the Supervisory Committee for handling. Later, on April 20th, Zhang Rongchu published an announcement in various newspapers in the city, painfully recounting the causes and consequences of his failure in managing the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Company. Another temporary emergency Standing Committee meeting was convened at 2:00 PM that afternoon, attended by all members of the Standing Committee for discussion. It was resolved that since the case had already been referred to the Supervisory Committee for thorough investigation in accordance with the previous resolution, so that it could be handled according to law, the Chamber of Commerce should issue a statement regarding the handling progress and the fact that Zhang Bofang was not a staff member of the Chamber and had not taken any files for investigation. This statement was published in various newspapers in the city on April 21st.

Letter from the Supervisory Committee

Received your confidential letter of the 18th of this month, stating that Executive Committee member Zheng Chengqing allegedly borrowed the name of the Chamber to pretextually investigate, requesting a thorough investigation, etc. Approved. A temporary meeting was convened on the 21st of this month, and it was resolved to publicly nominate Committee member Pei Yunqing to investigate and report in detail before making a decision on how to handle the matter. On the 23rd of this month, the investigative report of Committee member Pei Yunqing was received. Further meetings were convened on the 27th and 30th for discussion. It was unanimously agreed that, according to Zheng Chengqing's statement, the report on the investigation of the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Company and the summary signed by Chairman Yu were admitted to be forgeries. Regardless of whether he was motivated by patriotism or for the convenience of the investigation, the procedures were all improper, and he could hardly avoid the suspicion of pretext. Although he did not set foot in the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Company or contact Zhang Rongchu, after reviewing the statements of Zhang Bofang and Zhang Rongchu, it could be inferred that he had not had any relationship with Zhang Rongchu. However, Zheng's position as an Executive Committee member of the Chamber and the fact of this pretext created doubts from the outside world, which inevitably harmed the reputation of the Chamber. His improper behavior was indeed inexcusable. According to Zhang Bofang's statement, he admitted to sending a letter to Zhang Rongchu and carrying forged documents to the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Company. Zhang Rongchu claimed that he was being held hostage and intended to solicit rewards, while Zhang Bofang claimed that he was not involved with others and intended to ingratiate himself. Although the two sides held different views, regardless of the truth of their statements, the fact that he carried forged documents to make a point and had some ulterior motive was obvious and undeniable. Regardless of what he said or whom he claimed to be, he should not have used forged documents as a tool to achieve any purpose. His actions were highly inappropriate and could not be left unaddressed. Zheng Chengqing is an Executive Committee member of the Chamber and should be dealt with in accordance with the Chamber of Commerce Law. Zhang Bofang is not a staff member of the Chamber and should be dealt with in a separate case. It was publicly resolved that Executive Committee member Zheng Chengqing should be subject to expulsion and dismissal in accordance with Articles 17 and 22, Clause 3 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, to be submitted to the General Meeting of Members for public resolution. The Zhang Bofang portion should be handled separately by the Executive Committee based on the Chamber's investigation report. In addition to the decisions made within the scope of the Supervisory Committee's authority as mentioned above, the Executive Committee should make a public resolution on how to handle other legal matters.

Chamber of Commerce Law Provisions

Article 17 of the Chamber of Commerce Law states, "If a member representative engages in improper conduct that harms the reputation and credit of the Chamber of Commerce, they may be expelled by a resolution of the General Meeting of Members and the member who appointed them shall be notified. A member representative who has been expelled shall not be eligible to serve as a member representative for three years from the date of expulsion." Article 22, Clause 3 of the Chamber of Commerce Law stipulates, "If, in the performance of their duties, they violate laws or regulations, engage in embezzlement and bribery, or engage in other major improper conduct, they shall be dismissed by a resolution of the General Meeting of Members, or dismissed by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce or the highest local administrative authority."

Supervisory Committee Meetings

The Supervisory Committee of the Chamber held three temporary meetings regarding this case, all chaired by Committee member Du Yuesheng. The resolutions were as follows: First resolution of the April 21st meeting: It was resolved that this case is of great importance and should be thoroughly investigated and handled according to law. Committee member Pei Yunqing was publicly nominated to investigate and report in detail before making a decision on how to handle the matter. Second resolution of the April 27th meeting: It was resolved that the conduct of Executive Committee member Zheng Chengqing should be handled in accordance with Articles 17 and 22 of the Chamber of Commerce Law. Zhang Bofang is not a staff member of the Chamber and should be handled separately by the Chamber. Committee member Fang Jiaobo was first nominated to draft a response to the Executive Committee, and then a meeting would be held to make a decision. Third resolution of the April 30th meeting: It was resolved to adopt the principle decided at the previous meeting and to pass the draft letter prepared by Committee member Fang Jiaobo, and to reply to the Executive Committee on the same day.

Ministry of Transportation Replies to Chamber of Commerce Regarding Request to Lower Pacific Telegraph Rates: Sino-US Rates Are Already Low, Further Reduction Is Difficult to Implement 71

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Sino-American Trade Association, the China Branch of the International Chamber of Commerce, and the China International Trade Association previously submitted a petition to the Ministry of Transportation of the Executive Yuan to reduce Pacific telegraph rates to facilitate foreign trade. Yesterday, the Ministry of Transportation issued document Dian Zi No. 951, stating: Received your petition. After careful consideration by the Ministry regarding the request to reduce Pacific telegraph rates, the reply is as follows: The requested reduction in Pacific telegraph rates presumably refers to telegrams sent to the Americas. An examination of telegrams sent from Asian countries to the Americas reveals that the charging method is based on the rate to San Francisco as the base rate, with additional onward transmission fees for locations beyond San Francisco in the Americas. The current rate from our country to San Francisco is 3 gold francs and 75 centimes per word (code word rates are charged at 60% of the ordinary telegram rate). Compared to the standard of our country's current international telegraph rates, this is already relatively low. For example, the rate from our country to Java is 3 gold francs and 20 centimes per word, to Honolulu it is 3 gold francs and 47 centimes per word, and to Melbourne, Australia it is 3 gold francs and 62.5 centimes per word. A brief comparison of the distances and rates of the above locations will reveal that the rate to San Francisco is already difficult to reduce further. Your petition states that the rate from Japan to San Francisco is only 2 gold francs and 05 centimes per word, and from Luzon it is only 2 gold francs and 65 centimes per word, indicating that our country's rate is higher than other countries. An investigation reveals that the rate from Japan to San Francisco is 3 gold francs and 05 centimes per word, not 2 gold francs and 05 centimes per word. This rate has been confirmed by a telegram reply from the Tokyo Radio Station to the Ministry's International Radio Station. The rate from Luzon to San Francisco is indeed 2 gold francs and 65 centimes per word. However, the above two locations are closer to San Francisco, so their rates are naturally lower. A comparison of the rates required for sending telegrams from our country to Japan or Luzon with the rates from the above two locations to San Francisco is listed below:

Location | Rate per Word (Gold Francs)

Shanghai - San Francisco | 3.75

Shanghai - Japan | 0.5

Japan - San Francisco | 3.05

Shanghai - Japan - San Francisco | 3.80

Shanghai - Luzon | 1.00

Luzon - San Francisco | 2.65

Shanghai - Luzon - San Francisco | 3.65

The above table shows that the claim in your petition that our country's rate is higher than other countries is actually incorrect. Furthermore, international telegraph rates should be based on gold francs in accordance with the provisions of the International Telecommunications Convention. However, when collecting fees from the public, each country calculates them in terms of its own currency system. In countries that use the gold standard, a relatively stable exchange rate can be determined by comparing the weight of pure gold contained in a gold franc with the weight of pure gold contained in the country's legal currency. In countries that use the silver standard, the above exchange rate must change with the fluctuations of the price of gold, so it must be revised frequently. The reason why our country's international telegraph rate cannot be as stable as Japan's is this. An examination reveals that telegrams currently sent from our country to the Americas are handled by the Ministry's International Radio Station in Shanghai when transmitted by wireless radio, but in San Francisco, they are handled by the American Wireless Radio Transportation Company and the Mackay Company. When transmitted by submarine cable, they are handled by the Great Eastern, Great Northern, or Pacific Submarine Cable Telegraph Offices under the Ministry's jurisdiction in Shanghai, but the above submarine cables are still the property of the Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific companies. If rates need to be reduced, the consent of the above companies must be obtained first, which cannot be determined solely by the Ministry. In short, telecommunications is a public utility, and fees should be kept as low as possible within a reasonable range in order to benefit the public. Reducing international rates can promote trade and assist propaganda, and the Ministry is paying close attention. However, because there are many international communication locations, and the rate and method of apportioning fees are extremely complex, any increase or decrease in the rate at any one location can have a huge impact on the Ministry's telecommunications revenue. Therefore, a comprehensive plan must be carefully considered and decided. Sino-US rates are already low according to the current international telegraph charging standards, and the request for a further reduction is temporarily difficult to implement. Please be informed. This reply.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce: Instructs That Stamps Should Be Affixed to Delivery-for-Inspection Slips 72

Regarding the affixing of stamps to delivery-for-inspection slips, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, based on the instructions of the Ministry of Finance, replied to a letter from Futai Xiang Silk Store, stating: In response to your letter of the 30th of this month, your firm has a practice of delivering goods for inspection, and a delivery-for-inspection slip is attached when delivering the goods, stating the quantity and price of the goods. You ask whether stamps should be affixed to these delivery-for-inspection slips. Regarding this matter, the Chamber of Commerce received instructions from the Ministry of Finance, document Shui Zi No. 7298, on September 30th of last year, stating that the difference between a delivery-for-inspection slip and a shipping invoice depends on whether the transaction is completed or not. However, whether the goods delivered are sold or whether a portion is returned is not known to any third party other than the store delivering the goods and the customer. Since this delivery-for-inspection slip contains the name, quantity, and value of the goods, and is issued with the goods, it is no different in nature from a shipping invoice and should be affixed with stamps to prevent taking advantage. Since the Ministry of Finance has interpreted it in this way, it is appropriate for your store to affix stamps to the delivery-for-inspection slips. If a certain amount is sold and a certain amount is returned, this can be noted on the delivery-for-inspection slip, and this delivery-for-inspection slip can also serve as an invoice, without having to worry about opening invoices and affixing stamps twice for one shipment. As for those that are returned in full, there is no remedy.

According to the Continental News, Judge Helmick, Chief Judge of the United States Court for China, appointed lawyer Dr. Schlette as the liquidator of three companies, including the American Oriental Banking Corporation, on Friday, to replace Mr. Hoeff, who passed away in the United States. In addition, the assets of the Probst Field Land Company are now of little value, and it is feared that the debts to creditors will be difficult to repay. He intends to make every effort to collect debts owed to the three companies by various customers before the end of 1936, and to continue paying out to creditors in order to conclude the liquidation affairs in early 1937. As for the Probst Field Land Company, it is now being carefully managed by the custodian, striving for frugality. The protection of creditors is better than it was before the company was taken over by the custodian. The interests of creditors depend on the value of Shanghai real estate. It is not yet possible to decide whether the company will be reorganized.

Jin Shi Eats Without Money, Stabs His Father-in-Law with a Knife: A Drama of Utter Despair 78

Yue Wengshi, a woman from Ningbo, is 40 years old and makes a living by setting up a food stall at the intersection of East Qiujiang Road. A Cantonese worker named Jin Shi, 30 years old, lives at No. 10 Fuanli, Xiangshan Road, and relies on weaving for a living. Because his income is very small, he always eats two meals a day at Yue Wengshi's food stall. The day before yesterday, Jin Shi had no money, so he pawned his old woolen hat with Mrs. Yue. Yesterday at lunchtime, Jin went to buy food again, totaling 340 wen. At that time, he paid Mrs. Yue 2 jiao of silver. Yue Wengshi said that the two days of meals totaled more than 600 wen, so she returned the woolen hat that was pawned the day before and asked Jin to pay the difference. Unexpectedly, Jin insisted on using the woolen hat to offset the previous day's food costs and then found 14 copper coins. However, Yue Wengshi firmly refused, and the two began to argue. Unexpectedly, Jin pulled out a knife from his sleeve and stabbed her in the shoulder. Blood immediately gushed out, and she cried for help. Nearby police officers arrived, arrested the suspect, and took him to the police station. Yue Wengshi was sent to the hospital for treatment.

The Cihai Dictionary Compiled and Published by the Zhonghua Book Company is Published on a Regular Basis, Ushering in a New Era for Chinese Dictionaries 79

The Cihai dictionary compiled and published by the Zhonghua Book Company has been released for pre-sale, attracting widespread attention. A reporter specifically visited the relevant individuals at the company to inquire about the dictionary's compilation process and main objectives. With the company's detailed explanation, we present the following introduction. According to them, this book was started in the first year of the Republic of China (1912) as a sequel to the Zhonghua Da Zidian (Great Dictionary of China). Those in charge were Xu Wugao, Shu Xincheng, Shen Gu, and Zhang Xiang. More than a hundred people successively contributed to the writing, and it took twenty years to complete the manuscript, ushering in a new era for Chinese dictionaries. In ancient China, there were no specialized dictionaries. Those that existed were based on semantic relationships, such as the Erya and Guangya, or based on phonetic relationships, such as the Guangyun and Jiyun. The former evolved into encyclopedic works, and the latter evolved into rhyme dictionaries. Generally, they could be used for literary embellishment but not for understanding principles through reading. In recent years, the creation of dictionaries has become convenient for scholars. However, Xu, Shu, and others believed that with the advancement of modern learning and arts, the changes in personnel, and the rapid pace of metabolism, the propagation and evolution of language were also advancing rapidly, changing daily. If they did not innovate and adapt to the times, the usefulness of dictionaries would eventually be exhausted. Therefore, they gathered like-minded individuals to discuss the format and created the Cihai dictionary. The following is a summary of its main points: (A) Word Selection: This book includes both single and compound words, old and new, aiming to serve the needs of the general public. The emergence of new words and the survival of old words are vast and numerous. Old words can be based on previous dictionaries and encyclopedias, but new words are difficult to collect. Extensive reading of new books and newspapers yielded many results at the beginning, but later, the additions were minimal. Sometimes, it was difficult to find even one or two words in an entire day. Moreover, for imported terms, the transliteration of sounds and meanings often overlapped and conflicted. Deciding what to include and exclude required much deliberation. Furthermore, for the same word, new and old interpretations differed, and usage varied. It was necessary to consider both aspects comprehensively. New developments or changes in events, as well as changes or additions to place names, had to be continuously revised and updated. Words that had already been selected for this book were revised or deleted within a few months, and drafts that had been finalized were repeatedly changed within a year. In total, the number of drafts written was more than 300,000. Including revisions and re-editions, it was close to 500,000. In the end, only slightly more than 100,000 entries were retained. The scope of selection can be divided into eight categories: Words commonly found in ancient texts; Important names, objects, and systems in history; New words that are widely circulated; Idioms and allusions commonly used in writing; Important terms used in agriculture, industry, commerce, and other sectors of society; Commonly used ancient and modern place names in writing; The most important famous people and famous works; Terms commonly seen and used in science and the arts. In addition, any needs related to learning and professional pursuits were also considered at all times. (B) Explanation: In this book, specialized sciences are written by experts. The selection and exclusion of entries have their own systems, and the proportion of each specialty is roughly the same. The method of description is also generally the same. Commonly seen daily words that do not belong to the scope of science may seem easy to understand at first glance but are difficult to clarify upon closer inspection, or they may have undergone changes and cannot be traced back to their origins. For these types of entries, it is necessary to search for the origins of events and provide detailed explanations. The meanings of words were explained differently by ancient people according to the context. This book explains old words based on ancient exegesis. However, when multiple theories are compiled into one meaning, efforts are made to integrate and understand them. When there are divergent views but the meaning and purpose are not significantly different, they are summarized into one entry. When necessary, the theories of various scholars are cited to distinguish their similarities and differences. Therefore, the creation and finalization of one entry often involves reviewing dozens of books, and the result is only a definition of a few words or an explanation of a few dozen or hundreds of words. Also, if the same entry contains meanings from both new and old disciplines, it must be comprehensively explained or marked separately, removing redundancies and combining differences before the final draft is obtained. As for those meanings that are indeed different, they are explained in separate sections according to the traces of their meaning changes. The meanings that are used by analogy are distinguished, and the meanings that are marked with pseudonyms are also distinguished. The entries that are related to each other strive for coherence. Therefore, when proofreading a word in this book, related entries are retrieved and reviewed one by one, and problems are solved simultaneously. (C) Citation and Annotation of Chapter Titles: In addition to entries taken from the original books, this book should also include entries from dictionaries and encyclopedias. In the past, the books cited by dictionaries and encyclopedias either only listed the book name or also included the chapter title, which was inconsistent and easily led to errors. We have tried to find the original books based on the book names and chapter titles listed in various books, but often they do not match. The ancient books cited in this book must be checked against the original books, and the chapter titles must be listed in detail to ensure that they can be found immediately and avoid disappointment. The detailed and brief content of related entries complements each other. If only the detailed explanation is in entry A and the explanation is brief in entries B, C, etc., then only the words "see entry A for details" or "refer to entry A" are listed under the explanation or entry to save space. (D) Punctuation: Most ancient Chinese books do not have punctuation, and the difficulty of phrasing and reading them has been debated for hundreds of years without a definitive answer. This book uses new-style punctuation to determine the phrasing. (E) Volume: The volume of this book contains more than 100,000 entries, with a total of 8 million words. Because of the use of new-style punctuation, it is time-consuming for typesetters and difficult to proofread. However, it is much more convenient for readers. The company considers this book to be a rare masterpiece in the recent Chinese publishing industry, so the price is specially reduced, and low-priced pre-sales are offered to promote its popularity. Sample pages are printed and available for inquiries from all sectors.

Page 16

Case of the Murder of Japanese Soldier Nakayama Hideo: Full Record of Yesterday's Trial and Testimony; Police First Requested the Release of Chen Rongsheng; Prosecution Against Ye Haisheng and Yang Wendao; Ye and Yang Confronted Each Other, Claiming Ignorance of the Reason; Chief Detective Investigating the Cause of the Assassination 80

Public Prosecution

Nakayama Hideo, a soldier of the Japanese Naval Landing Forces stationed in Shanghai, was shot and killed on Baole An Road on the night of November 9th of last year. The murderer fled the scene, and only a live pistol and a bullet casing were found at the scene of the incident. Only last month, the police of the Public Concession successively arrested three suspects: Yang Wendao, chairman of the Guangdong Tongren Association; Ye Haisheng (nickname: Little Guangdong), a member of the association; and Chen Rongsheng. A book containing a hollowed-out space for a pistol was found in Yang's home. They were sent to the First Special District Court for investigation. Because the case was important, spectators were prohibited, so the reports in the newspapers were brief. Now, the police have formally filed a public prosecution against Yang and Ye.

Public Hearing

The day before yesterday, at 2:00 PM, Criminal Court President Qian Hongye, together with Judges Feng Shide and Xiao Xiexi, formed a collegial panel in the First Court to conduct a public hearing. The ban on publication was also lifted. After 1:00 PM, those who went to observe the hearing came one after another. The municipal government and the municipal Public Security Bureau attached great importance to it. Mayor Wu specially sent Secretary-General Zhang Tingrong, and Public Security Bureau Chief Cai sent Third Section Chief Huang Hua to the court to observe the hearing. The Japanese military headquarters stationed in Shanghai paid particular attention, sending five officers in military uniform with swords and four soldiers, supervised by a senior officer. The officers sat in the ordinary spectator seats, and the soldiers stood beside them. In addition, all Chinese, Western, and Japanese detectives involved in the case were present in court to be questioned. The atmosphere inside the courtroom was quite tense, and the order was very strict. Although it was a public trial, entry and exit still required inspection. Law enforcement officers and detectives were deployed from inside the court to the gate of the courthouse to maintain order. After the three judges took their seats, Prosecutor Zhang Zongru also attended the court to perform his duties. Lawyers Liang and Ru Bao-Yi represented the police in the prosecution. Since the defendants had not retained lawyers, the court appointed lawyers Fan Gang and Zhang Zhirang to defend them. Now, Yang Wendao has hired lawyers Jiang Yiping, Wu Baotai, and Ge Zhaoji to appear in court for his defense. President Qian first asked Yang, Chen, and Ye about their ages, hometowns, addresses, and occupations. Then, Lawyer Ru requested that Chen Rongsheng be released, stating that Chen had no criminal evidence in this case and therefore would not be prosecuted. The court ordered that he be released and, for the sake of caution, ordered all witnesses to be interrogated separately. Those who were to be questioned were temporarily asked to step aside to await their summons. Then, Lawyer Ru presented the facts of the crime committed by Yang and Ye.

Prosecution's Intent

Stating that, according to Article 271 of the Criminal Law, the defendants are accused of murder. A Japanese soldier named Nakayama Hideo was shot and killed with a pistol on Baole An Road at 9:00 PM on November 9th of last year. After investigation by the police, it was determined that Yang Wendao fired the shot, and Ye Haisheng was present to help commit the crime. The evidence is as follows: The medical report of the doctor who examined the deceased confirmed that he was killed by a pistol. A pistol was found at the scene of the incident that night. This gun was made in Italy, with the number 14246. Its caliber is .32. It was found by a Japanese patrolman in the Fengle Lane on North Sichuan Road. There were five bullets inside the gun, and another bullet had already been fired into the chamber. At the same time, another Japanese patrolman also found a bullet casing and a bullet that had been fired at the scene. A book was found in Yang Wendao's bedroom at No. 18, Tong'an Lane, Tangshan Road. This book was found by Japanese patrolman No. 134 under the clothes rack. It is called "Practical Physics." There was a hole in the book in the shape of a pistol. When the gun found at the scene was inserted into the hole, it fit perfectly. Moreover, the gun had been stored in the hole for a long time, so the Western license number and texture on the gun were deeply imprinted on the book page. This imprint has been photographed and is easy to examine. After Yang was arrested, he admitted to the court that the book was his, but he said that the book was picked up from outside by his child, and he had borrowed a "Dimeng" (transliteration) brand pistol from his friend Li, and had obtained a gun license from the Public Works Department. The hole in the book was for storing the borrowed gun. After investigation by the police, it was learned that Li's gun had been lent to Xu Xiangxing, so the gun was retrieved from Xu. The gun number was 87958, while the gun license that Yang had donated in previous years was 2617. However, the gun did not fit into the hole in the book, so Yang's statement that the hole in the book was for storing the Dimeng brand pistol and not the "Western Pi" brand pistol was unbelievable. During the second interrogation, Yang's father stated that the book found was not the original book found in his home. Although there was a book that was searched at that time, it was not the book presented now. The previous and subsequent statements contradicted each other, which shows that the defendant had a great relationship with the "Western Pi" brand pistol found at the scene. As for Ye Haisheng, after being arrested, he wrote a confession in the police station, in which he confessed that Yang had discussed the matter with him beforehand, witnessed Yang firing the gun, and then fled separately. If his confession is true, then the murder committed by the two defendants is undoubtedly true. The witness Zeng Yun has a deep understanding of the murder weapon. Now he has been summoned with other witnesses, and they should be investigated one by one, and the two pistols, bullets, bullet casings, and photos and other exhibits should be submitted to the case.

Detectives' Report

Then, the detectives in charge of the case reported the situation of the investigation to the court in order. First, the Japanese deputy head of the Jiaxing Road police station translated. He said that at 11:40 PM on November 9th of last year, he learned of the consumption that Nakayama Hideo was murdered, and he went to Fengle Lane to investigate. He found a pistol near the residence of the Sige people in the lane and brought it back to the police station. At that time, he did not pay attention to whether there were any fingerprints left on the gun. Next, Western Detective Hart of the Dixiwei Road police station translated. He said that he went to the scene of the incident at 9:05 PM on the same night. By the time, the body had been moved away, but blood stains remained on the ground. The place was 29 feet and 6 inches away from Baole An Road, and a little south was where the pistol bullet found in Fengle Lane was more than four feet away from the blood site. The place where the body fell was 13 feet away from the steps along Baole An Road. After Nakayama was shot, he did not die immediately, but died at the Japanese Marine Corps Hospital at 1:00 AM the next morning. All guns and bullets will be proven by firearms experts separately. Then, Western Detective Oak of the Firearms Inspection Department reported the process of inspecting the pistol bullets, translated by interpreter Jiang Baoliang. According to him, after inspecting the four-pi brand pistol on November 10th of last year, he felt that its machinery was complete and it had been used recently. He immediately test-fired it with live ammunition, and the shape of the bullet casing ejected was the same as the shape of the bullet casing handed over for inspection. Therefore, it can be determined that the bullet casing was indeed fired from the gun. He also submitted an enlarged photo of the gun bullet to the case. Then, Western Deputy Detective Haisheng reported on the inspection of the fingerprints, saying that since the gun was steel and the paint had not completely fallen off, it would not leave any fingerprints even if it was held by someone's hand. Then, Japanese patrolman No. 61 and Japanese detective No. 83 of the Dixiwei Road police station separately reported that at about 10:00 PM on November 9th, they found a bullet and a bullet casing that had been fired near the scene of the incident. The bullet was still stained with blood. Then, Japanese patrolman No. 160 proved that he went to Yang Wendao's house at No. 18, Tong'an Lane, Tangshan Road with Chinese and Western detectives at 4:00 PM on April 19th of this year and searched the bottom of the clothes rack in Yang's bedroom for a book. Western Detective Hart then translated, saying that when the Japanese patrolman discovered the book, all the personnel who were searching at the same time had witnessed it, and he took the book from the Japanese patrolman and took it back to the police station during the search. Yang Wendao glanced at it, and immediately admitted that the book was his, and also said that there was a hole in the book for storing a pistol. Later, it was learned that Yang had borrowed a pistol from Li, and then Li lent it to Xu Xiangxing. Now the gun has been retrieved, but the size of the hole in the book is not suitable, which is a subtle indication that the hole was not storing Li's gun.

Ye Haisheng's Confession

The court then questioned the defendant Ye Haisheng, who confessed that he was 28 years old, from Guangdong, and working as a dance hall leader, living at No. 22, Qingdao Cangku Road. He often went to and from Shanghai Qing. This time, he went to Qing to open a dance hall last November. The capital was provided by my wife Chen Guizhen, who used to be a dancer. I met her in the dance hall. Chen once followed Huang Jinrong. I only bonded with her when I went to Qingdao the year before last. She has been a dancer for eight years and has quite a lot of savings. On November 7th of last year, Yang Wendao came to me, but I didn't go to his house. Yang's house is on Tangshan Road, I have been there several times before. I didn't go this time, so Yang came to visit me again at the door of the Moon Palace Hotel on North Sichuan Road at 7:00 PM on the 9th, along with the Korean Jack. I have a gap with Jack and he is violent. I didn't want to see him, so I told Yang. Yang told me not to be afraid of him and said that he was going to kill a Japanese person and invited me to go with him. After only these words, I followed him. When we arrived at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Baole An Road, Yang suddenly went ahead, Jack blocked it, and I was in the rear. When we reached the corner, we saw a Japanese soldier coming towards us, and we saw Yang flipping through the book he was carrying, and then we heard a bang. We scattered and fled. Yang first formed the Hongshun Mutual Aid Association, and he was the chairman. I joined the association in the 22nd year as a member. Later, the Hongshun Association disbanded, and Yang formed the Tongren Association, and still served as chairman. I was also a member. The former members of the association were also members of Hongshun, so we knew each other. At that time, I gambled and defrauded the deposit of his second landlord, and I also opened a Yanzike, and someone reported it to the association, so we fought twice. I have never used a pistol to pledge 25 yuan to him.

Witness Zeng Yuan

The court then summoned the witness Zeng Yuan, who confessed that he lived at No. 6, Fengle Lane, Baole An Road, and worked as a lunch box maker. He used to be a clerk at Taikoo, and he knew Yang Wendao because he worked at the Taikoo warehouse. He knew Ye in the dance hall. Ye's economic situation is not very clear. At the end of September last year, Ye asked for 25 yuan, but I refused because he had no guarantor. Two days later, Ye came again with a pistol to pledge. My wife thought it was dangerous and told me to reject it. I never fought with Ye. Ye heard the words and immediately confronted me, but he denied that he had fought, and insisted that Ye had used a pistol to pledge the deposit without success. He also said that in December, a friend surnamed Chen came to visit, and accidentally flipping through the application for a loan, he caught a glimpse of Ye, so he talked about it. Unexpectedly, Chen told the detectives. In January of this year, detectives came to inquire and I recognized that one of the several pistols was the one Ye had used to borrow money, because there were two circles on the face of the gun, so I could still recognize it. As for Ye's loan application, it has been torn up with other discarded ones. At this time, the defendant's lawyer Wan Zhaoji wanted to state the details of the situation, but it was quite complicated. Then the defendant's lawyer Jiang Yiping requested the court to allow the details that Lawyer Ge wanted to say to be submitted in writing later, so as not to disclose the secret and save time.

Yang Wendao's Confession

The court then questioned the defendant Yang Wendao, who confessed that he was the chairman of the Hongshun and Tongren Associations, and Ye was a member of Hongshun. I used to work at Taikoo, so I knew Zeng Yuan. The book found in my house is not the book presented to the case. The reason why I confessed that the book presented to the case was found in my house during the first trial was because I didn't look closely at the time, and the two books were similar in form. My book also had a hole, which contained a pistol that I borrowed from Li Mu and had a license donated to the Public Works Department. I don't know the number and brand of the gun now. I did not send a letter to Ye Haisheng on November 7th, and I did not invite Ye Haisheng to shoot and kill Japanese soldiers with the Korean at night on the 9th. I don't know why Ye said this now. The court then ordered Ye and Yang to confront each other. Ye repeated the details he had confessed, but Yang still said that this was not the case, but was being falsely accused by him and wanted to shift the blame to me, but I have no feud with Ye. The court then questioned Ye again and instructed him to explain the reason for the murder. Unexpectedly, Ye claimed that he did not know the reason either. At that time, Yang only said that he was going to kill a Japanese person, and then he followed him. He did not meet Yang afterwards.

Zhang Kaiyuan's Confession

The court also summoned the witness Zhang Kaiyuan, a Ningbo native, who confessed that he founded a dance school and hired Ye to teach dance, so he knew him. On the night of November 29th, he saw Ye, the Korean Jack, and another person walking on the road. Not long after, I heard people in the Nanyang Dance Hall say that a Japanese soldier had been shot and killed. At that time, I suspected that Ye and others were responsible. When Jack was detained by the Japanese consulate, I talked about it with people and was heard by the detectives. Now I am being summoned to testify, etc. Ye confronted Zhang, saying that the clothes he was wearing that night were inconsistent. After questioning, the court ordered Western Detective Hart to base his report on the reason for the death of the deceased. He said that he was still investigating, and that his actions that day had been investigated. The deceased was originally full of duties and was planning to return to his country. That afternoon, he first played at No. 33, Yokohama Bridge. A Japanese woman lived in that house. Then he re-entered No. 27. He resigned at about 8:30. Judging from his route, it seemed that he was going back to camp, so he walked slowly along North Sichuan Road to Baole An Road and was killed. It was already five o'clock, and President Qian instructed to reschedule the trial to Wednesday afternoon next week. Yang and Ye were still escorted back to the police station in a prison car by detectives to be detained.

Republic Road Robbery at Rice Store - Box Cannon Injures Western Detective - Police Detectives Bravely Give Chase... Gang Fires Along the Way - Left Bandit Climbs onto Rooftop to Escape... Remaining Bandits and Loot Captured 82

Around 4:30 PM the day before yesterday, at the Jin Sheng Chang Rice Store, a three-bay shop located at numbers 46, 48, and 50 near the Xiaocai Market on Gonghe Road in Zhabei, a young apprentice named Cai Deyang, aged nineteen and from Gaoqiao in Pudong, arrived at the store on a bicycle from the old store on Wuchang Road in the concession (Jin Sheng Rice Store) to collect accounts. As he stepped out of the store, preparing to mount his bicycle, a tall bandit wearing a grey cloth long gown and speaking with a Jiangbei accent appeared beside him. The bandit pulled out a box cannon, saying, "Be sensible!" and snatched a package of silver dollar fractional notes, totaling forty-nine dollars and ten cents, from the apprentice's outer pocket. Apparently, the bandit didn't realize they were fractional notes or how much they amounted to, so he fled north along Datong Road and Haichang Road with the loot. Upon entering the crowd, the bandit handed the stolen money and box cannon to another bandit. Store employees who witnessed the event blew a police whistle and gave chase. Police officer Du Yikuan, who was on duty at post number 14, and Ning Zhenlin, from neighboring post number 15, hearing the alarm, pursued the bandits frantically. At the intersection of Datong Road and Haichang Road, one of the bandits, wearing a blue cloth long gown, fired a box cannon at Officer Ning, but luckily missed. The bandits then split up and fled along Haichang Road, firing continuously to resist arrest. At this time, Bao Ziying, the captain of the Xinzha Detective Squad, led team leader Li Shouchang and detectives Lü Qingkang, Liu Tongjie, Sun Youzhi, and Zhang Shuwen in a brave pursuit. The first team of the security forces also assisted in the capture. The bandits crossed bamboo fences into small paths northwards, then fled wildly along the railway towards the Sun Temple. One bandit lost a pair of Zhigong呢shoes while running. The police officers at the Sun Temple post, hearing the whistle, blocked the escape route. Officer Du then grabbed the bandit carrying the stolen money and the shoe, and took him back to the team for interrogation. The bandit confessed to being Wang Renfu, aged twenty-six, from Funing, residing in a straw shack in Caojiadu. He admitted that he and his accomplices Jiang Zhengming and Zuo Zhengzhong had brought a box cannon and robbed the rice store on Gonghe Road of its account money. He stated that the box cannon had been handed to Zuo, and that Zuo and Jiang had fled together, living at number 1, Yuandian Lane, Zhoujiazui Road in the concession, and offered to lead them to their arrest. After the team obtained this confession, in addition to the original officers Liu Tongjie and Lü Qingkang, they dispatched Mao Gongzhao, Liu Bingrong, Yuan Weishu, and Gao Changgui to collaborate with the Jiaxing Road Police Station. At 6:30 PM that day, they sent Western detective Ai'erde Si from the 4th team and Chinese detective Mu Jin Yangwu number 10, and Chinese detective Gu Wenyao from the 157th team to Yuandian Lane number 2, Zhoujiazui Road, for a secret arrest. A woman answered the door. The detectives stopped her immediately. Western detective Ai'erde Si was the first to go upstairs, but the bandit Zuo Zhengzhong had already noticed them and fired a box cannon at the Western detective, injuring his right arm. Zuo then carrying the gun leaped onto the roof to escape. Hearing the sound, the detectives downstairs rushed upstairs, but Zuo had already disappeared. They arrested Jiang Zhengming and the woman, Chen Zhou shi. The injured Western detective was taken to the hospital in an ambulance summoned by the police station. Inside the house, they found the original stolen fractional notes totaling twenty-three dollars and ninety cents, fifteen bullets, one magazine, two seals, fourteen pawn tickets, and sixty fake pearls, all of which were taken to the police station. After a brief interrogation by the police chief, the case was handed over to the detectives of the Public Security Bureau to be taken back to Zhabei for further investigation. Jiang Zhengming confessed to being thirty-four years old, from Funing, and residing at number 2 Yuandian Lane, Zhoujiazui Road, stating that he was the second landlord, etc. Chen Zhou shi confessed to being thirty-two years old and a hired servant, etc. It is also reported that the gang is suspected of other crimes and is currently under investigation.

Ningbo Native Association Calls Emergency Meeting Regarding the Relocation of Graves in Ningbo - Public Outrage, Crowded Gallery - Telegrams Sent to Central and Provincial Governments Requesting Rectification 84

The Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai, concerned about the hasty relocation of graves in various towns and villages in Ningbo, which has led to incidents of graves being mistakenly exhumed, such as the ancestral grave of the former director of the Palace Museum and the grave of the elder brother of Zhao Bonian, the former speaker of the Yin County Assembly, both being relocated by the township governments due to failure to register in time, and numerous similar cases, and furthermore, the contractors responsible for the relocation were using small coffins to hold the remains of four or five bodies, causing dismemberment and desecration, which was too ghastly to bear. At the request of the Ningbo people, the association telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Department of Civil Affairs, requesting rectification. They received a reply from the provincial government stating that graves that had been buried for a long time would be exempt from relocation, as previously reported. However, the Yin County Government continued to issue notices urging relocation and did not exclude existing graves, causing great panic among the local people and the Ningbo people in Shanghai, who pleaded for assistance. Considering the urgency of the matter, the association convened an emergency meeting of the executive and supervisory committees yesterday afternoon. The Ningbo people were extremely concerned about this case, and hundreds of them gathered at the association to listen in. The meeting room was overcrowded, and the atmosphere was tense, with the public feeling extremely outraged. The meeting adjourned at over 7 PM. The names of the committee members present, as recorded, include Yu Qiaqing, Fang Jiaobo, Yuan Ludeng, Wang Boyuan, Qin Runqing, Jin Runxiang, and over fifty others. It was resolved to send telegrams to the provincial government and Chairman Jiang of the Executive Yuan requesting rectification and to appoint seven committee members to form a special committee to handle the case.
