China Travel Service Organizes a European Tour to Attend the World Games 93

The upcoming World Games are scheduled to be held in Berlin, Germany, from August 1st to 16th of this year. The Chinese delegation, consisting of 100 people, has entrusted China Travel Service with the purchase of tickets, transportation of luggage, and processing of passports and various procedures through the National Sports Association. The decision has been made to depart from Shanghai on the Italian postal ship Conte Verde on June 26th, disembarking in Venice, Italy, and then transferring by train to Germany. After the closing of the World Games, they will return home on the Conte Rosso, departing from Italy on September 9th, arriving in Hong Kong on the 25th of the same month, and arriving in Shanghai on the 27th. Considering that Europeans and Americans often come in groups to visit our country's major cities to learn about our customs and culture and to investigate commercial conditions for reference upon returning home, and that our people rarely undertake such grand tours, the company, based on its commitment to serving travelers, is organizing a tour group to attend the World Games and travel to Europe. The costs will be kept to a minimum, and specialists will be assigned to accompany the group. This will enable those in the country who wish to attend the World Games to travel in groups, to witness the competition of the world's athletes, and to take the opportunity to visit the capitals and scenic areas of European countries, gaining a deep understanding of the ancient and modern culture of those countries. This is truly killing several birds with one stone. The tour is scheduled to depart with the delegation on the same ship and return to Shanghai on the same ship, with a total duration of three months and one day, and 46 days of travel in Europe. In addition to attending the World Games, the tour will visit Venice, Vienna, the capital of the Czech Republic, the Netherlands, London, Brussels, Paris, Geneva, Nice, Monte Carlo, Genoa, Rome, and Naples. As for the ports along the Italian postal route, including Hong Kong, Singapore, Colombo, and Little Luzon, it is planned to disembark and travel by car, with the length of time depending on the time the ship docks. According to the above itinerary, the cost includes passage in economy class, accommodation in second-class hotels, train tickets, and entrance tickets to the venues for the World Games and various art galleries and theaters, all limited to second class. Other expenses, such as luggage transportation and local guides, are included. The cost is £155 per person. Those who wish to upgrade to first-class ship and first-class hotels will need to pay £280 per person. Personal expenses, tips on the ship, and passport fees are not included. The number of participants is capped at 20 and a minimum of 10. Those who wish to join the tour or obtain detailed information should contact China Travel Service at number 420, Sichuan Road.

The term "neurasthenia," I think you have often heard of it. It is extremely popular among young people. Moreover, not only young people, but also older and middle-aged people often suffer from neurasthenia. Therefore, this disease is one of the most common diseases in modern civilized society. It is often found in people who are mentally depressed, physically and mentally overworked, or who use their energy excessively, and who have unlimited sexual intercourse and masturbation. Now I will describe the symptoms of this disease and its general treatment methods as follows:

There are many different symptoms of neurasthenia, which can be divided into two main categories: congenital and acquired.

Acquired Neurasthenia

Generally, the so-called neurasthenia mostly refers to acquired neurasthenia. The main symptoms of this disease are: sleep disorders, scattered attention, memory loss, heaviness of the head, hyperreflexia, etc. In addition, there are symptoms such as headache, fatigue, irritability, dizziness, and tinnitus.

Congenital Neurasthenia

Congenital neurasthenia is also called physical weakness or simply neurasthenia. There are mental symptoms from birth - especially the emotional and volitional symptoms are the most obvious. (Regarding emotions) Hypersensitivity, irritability, easy to anger, bad temper, unpleasantness, feelings of incompetence, inferiority, paying attention to trivial matters, nagging, obsessive ideas, phobias…

Regarding attention, lack of resistance, inability to endure Zhou's affairs, no thinking ability, slow decisions. Sometimes it presents an extroverted - aggressive personality, can become a fighter, agitator, and easily cause violence. If there is an introverted personality, it will present strange symptoms such as depression, world-weariness, pessimism, suicidal tendencies, and misanthropy.

The above is an overview of neurasthenia. The large number of symptoms and the great harm can be inferred from this.

Dietary Management of Neurasthenia

First, you must first quit mental and physical overwork, and appreciate the scenery of mountains and rivers to broaden your mind, rest, get enough sleep, take walks in the suburbs, breathe fresh air, and get close to the sunlight to keep your body and mind quiet. Smoking and drinking are strictly prohibited, and tea, coffee, etc. must be restricted. Regarding food, avoid salty, spicy, mustard, and other stimulating foods. Other meats and foods that are too stimulating and exciting should also be paid special attention to.

Daily life must also be regular and disciplined. Getting up, eating, bathing, walking, exercising, and resting must all be scheduled at appropriate times. It is strictly forbidden to go to bed late, or to enter game halls, dance halls, obscene conversations, books, etc. The eyes must also avoid seeing them. The excitement of sexual desire and the bad habit of masturbation must be restrained or quit.

World University Games Football Team Departed Yesterday for Foreign Expedition 111

A Group of Twenty Set Sail on French Mail Steamer, First to Undertake Training Matches in Southeast Asia

The Chinese football team representing our country at the World University Games, a group of twenty led by Rong Qizhao and Yan Chengkun, departed yesterday at 4 PM on the French mail steamer "Aramis." Zhou Jiaqi and Shi Zhaokang of the China National Amateur Athletic Federation, along with Zhou Xianyan, Chen Zhenxiang, Zhong Yongsen from the local football community, team members, and reporters from various newspapers, numbering in the dozens, gathered at the wharf to see them off. Details of the departure are recorded as follows:

Heading First to Southeast Asia: For the sake of thorough training, the football team is departing in advance to Southeast Asia for practice matches. The planned locations include Saigon, Java, Medan, Sumatra, Malaysia, Burma, and India, with a total of thirty matches planned for training. They are scheduled to convene in Bombay on July 8, joining other athletes to board the Italian mail steamer "Conte Verde" to travel to Germany via Italy, to attend the Games. The final team roster will be determined after the training matches in Southeast Asia, based on the performance of each player.

Twenty Athletes Departed: The group that departed yesterday included leaders Yan Chengkun and Rong Qizhao, captain Li Huitang, and players Bao Jia, Tan Jiangbai, Li Tiansheng, Huang Meishun, Li Guowei, Chen Zhenhe, Liang Shutang, Feng Jingxiang, Ye Beihua, Zheng Jiliang, Yang Shuiyi, Zhang Xianyuan, Sun Jinshun, Zhuo Shijin, Cao Guicheng, and Jia Youliang, totaling twenty. Additional team members Huang Jiliang, Mai Zhaohan, Cai Wenli, and Xu Yahui will join them on later voyages from Hong Kong and Singapore.

Farewell Banquet at the Da Dong Restaurant: The China National Amateur Athletic Federation hosted a farewell banquet at the Da Dong Restaurant on Friday evening, the first of the month, to bid farewell to the World University Games team and to welcome the players from the foreign teams participating in the competition in this city. Attendees included the entire World University Games team and the players from the three French, Portuguese, and Western United teams, bringing together the best Chinese and foreign football players in the city. Key officials from the Football Association and newspaper reporters were also invited to the banquet. During the banquet, Tu Zhengting, chairman of the Athletic Federation, delivered a speech wishing the team success. Shen Siliang spoke, encouraging the players to bear the great responsibility and expressing gratitude for the cooperation of the press. Representatives from the foreign teams also delivered congratulatory speeches. Sun Daosheng, a reporter from this newspaper, delivered a congratulatory farewell speech. Finally, team captain Li Huitang gave a speech of thanks, and the banquet concluded.

Japanese Cultural Enterprise Department Establishes Oriental Library in Peiping 128

Opening expenses of 60,000 yuan have been allocated, and personnel have been sent to Peiping for preparation. The selection of the library director and the appointment of staff require long-term consideration.

(Special dispatch from Peiping) The Japanese Cultural Enterprise Department plans to establish an Oriental Library in Peiping, with an opening cost of 60,000 yuan. Personnel have already been sent to Peiping to investigate suitable locations. According to news from educational circles who have studied in Japan, the Japanese Cultural Enterprise Department believes that although the national capital has moved south, Peiping remains the cultural center of China, and there are still many academic institutions in Peiping. The largest library in Peiping, the Peiping Library, has a large collection of ancient Chinese books and Western books, but relatively few Japanese books. Although the Peking University Library has Japanese literature, it is only for the use of teachers and students. The library of the Peking University Law and Commerce College also has a large collection of Japanese books, mostly on law, politics, and economics, but they are not accessible to people outside the university. The library that the Japanese Cultural Enterprise Department plans to establish will be open to the public. In addition to ancient books, it will comprehensively collect newly published Japanese books on social sciences, natural sciences, literature, philosophy, and education for public access. Funding is not an issue, but the selection of the library director and the appointment of staff require long-term consideration. As for the location, there are more schools in the western part of Peiping than in the eastern part, and most intellectuals outside the education sector also live in the Xidan Pailou and Xisi Pailou areas, so the Oriental Library is planned to be located in the western part of the city.

Lu Province Increases Funding for Education 132

Jinan Dispatch, Last year, the province expanded compulsory education, and more than 2,000 short-term elementary schools were added throughout the province, with excellent results. Now, the Ministry of Education has instructed the provincial government to list compulsory education as the central task, and when preparing the budget for the 25th year, to increase the funding for compulsory education by more than double that of the previous year, and to formulate an implementation plan and report the exact amount of increased funding to the Ministry of Education for approval before May 15, etc. The Department of Education believes that the Ministry has clearly stipulated that the principle is that half of the funding for compulsory education in each province should be raised by the provinces themselves. Jiangsu, Hebei, Henan, and Anhui provinces have all allocated large sums of money from their provincial treasuries to be used specifically for compulsory education. The funding for compulsory education in this province, in addition to the supplementary funding from the central government, is allocated from the compulsory education fund turned over to the province by various counties and the repayment of military funds from the 18th and 19th years, and no funds have been drawn from the provincial treasury. The budget for the 24th year lists 709,076 yuan. If the order from the Ministry of Education is followed, and the funding is doubled in the 25th year, it should be 1.41 million yuan. In addition to the 320,000 yuan or so that can be allocated from the repayment of military funds from the 18th and 19th years, and the 170,000 yuan that has been eroded from the compulsory education fund, there is still a shortfall of more than 920,000 yuan. Today (the 1st), the Director of Education He Siyuan of the Department of Education raised this issue at the provincial government's political meeting, requesting instructions on how to raise this 920,000+ yuan, as it concerns the future of compulsory education. After discussion, it was decided to hand over the matter to the Department of Finance and the Department of Education for consideration.

Jiang Kanghu Shortens Lecture Period 135

Jiang Kanghu's lecture series on Chinese Studies at the New World Company was originally scheduled for fifty-two lectures, to be completed in exactly one year. It is now heard that Jiang is shortening the lecture period because he has accepted an invitation from overseas Chinese in Canada and will be leaving the country for the United States soon. He will only give the first part, "Chinese History and Geography," in thirteen lectures. This afternoon at 3 p.m., he will still give the eleventh lecture at the New World Company, titled "The Chinese Mainland." He will give a detailed explanation of the development process of the Chinese mainland, the natural and human differences between the northern, central, northwestern, and southeastern provinces, and the evolution and development of major cities in each province. Those who wish to hear Jiang's great theories should not miss this opportunity.

Genius painter Liu Shi entered the Art Department of Japan University in the winter of 1933 to study painting, sculpture, and art history. After diligent research, he has achieved extremely high accomplishments. He has now returned to China on the Changxing Liner Asia Queen, arriving in Shanghai at 11 a.m. on May 4.

The Nanjing Municipal School for the Blind and Deaf has been running for many years and has achieved remarkable results. If any places in the country wish to establish blind education undertakings or need such special talents to run schools for blind children, please contact the school immediately.

Afterwards, trading remained active, but the market was hovering, only slightly lower than the initial opening. By the afternoon opening, the downward trend was somewhat stabilized, but trading was still lively. The market price for each month was similar to the morning closing price. Total turnover for the day reached one million, and the October contract was auctioned as usual, opening at 3.025 yuan and closing one cent higher, for a total decline of 1.5 cents.

Yesterday (the 2nd), the flour market reported that wheat prices in Chicago fell by 40 cents for near-term contracts and 20 cents for far-term contracts. Canadian wheat fell by 24 cents. By the afternoon opening, the number of factories exiting had slowed, but off-exchange selling was still enthusiastic. The June contract was previously inverted, with more selling, and was now equal to the July contract, reaching a low of 3.04 yuan, a sharp decline of 15 cents from the previous week's high. Although the other months also fell successively, the comparison was still moderate. The decline has been going on for two days since May, and according to the market situation, there are still signs of continued weakness.

Credo for Success 178

— A Teacher

Little friends! Here are a few creeds for success, which can serve as guidelines for our studies and work!

Do things in the clear-headed and refreshing morning; not in the exhausted late night.

With the spirit of hard work, the matter is already half successful.

Hands in pockets cannot climb the ladder.

Plan your work with all your mind; execute your plan with all your mind.

The solution to the matter lies only in your determination.

Do not only do ready-made things; be able to find things to do yourself.

Sitting and watching is not as good as taking action.

Absorb a large amount of knowledge, and chew it slowly.

People who are jealous of others' success will never succeed themselves.

An ambitious person does not necessarily do what they like; they only care about liking to do what should be done.

Correct thinking should be followed by action.

Use normal thinking to do extraordinary undertakings.

A genius is good at seizing opportunities already obtained.

Keep working hard at all times, and success is not far away.

How Big Is the Earth? 180

— By Xianweisheng

Little friends, you probably all know that the shape of the Earth is like a sphere. As for how big its circumference is? How many miles in total? Perhaps you haven't heard your teacher mention it yet. I'll write it down now and tell you!

From the South Pole, straight through the Earth's core to the North Pole, like drilling a hole straight through, is a total of 7,899 miles. From the east straight through the Earth's core to the west is a total of 7,925 miles! The circumference is a total of 24,850 miles.

Good Little Brother 181

— By Shi Yusheng

Good little brother, doesn't like to cry, he says: "Crying is surrendering; it cannot relieve our pain, nor can it bring us happiness!"

The rain beats down hard, the wind blows fiercely, the road is muddy and truly difficult to walk, making the tired person want to cry; but, good little brother, he is careful, takes steady steps, perks up his spirits and moves forward, and he eventually happily walks into the school gate.

Tired of reading books, laughter comes from the playground, good little brother also goes to relax, the ball just rolls over, he kicks it away happily, - "Whose ball is it, don't even ask, quickly pick it up and return it to us!" Several strong kids shout fiercely, a slap in the face makes good little brother hurt, this is really too unbearable, inevitably tears well up; but, good little brother, he asks the teacher to judge the matter, and from then on exercises his body, to build a foundation for self-improvement.

Good little brother, good little brother, in his eyes, there are no tears; in his mind, there is only struggle!

Foreign Doll 182

— By Wen Yuyang

Little friends, don't you like playing with foreign dolls very much? We can use melons and vegetables to make a foreign doll to play with! It looks very interesting.

If you want to make it to play with, you must first prepare the materials. One eggplant (purple), two round turnips, three cowhorn peppers (red), four green peppers (cut in the middle), five long turnips (very small), six bamboo skewers (four pieces). The size of the materials should be based on the size of the eggplant.

After preparing the materials, first insert Figure 1 and Figure 5 with bamboo skewers as shown in (Figure 1), then put Figure 4 on top of the two rounds as shown in (Figure 2) and insert them in the same way, and you will have a very interesting foreign doll.

What Kind of Person Will I Be in the Future? 183

— By Liu Dingjuan

(Thirteenth Place)

Generally, a person's ambition is very great at the beginning; but in the end, it is difficult for one or two out of ten people to achieve their goals. Investigating the reason for this, what is it? For the most part, they can only say it with their mouths, but they cannot truly bury their heads in hard work, which is truly the most laughable thing. You must know that no matter what matter, what desire, will never succeed by just talking about it, you must go and do it, and then you can succeed.

I have no extravagant desires. Now I only hope to be a good student and a good citizen in the future. Today's students are the good pillars of the country in the future, the good members of society, and the good children of the family. I dare to boldly say that among today's students, it is difficult to find three or four out of ten who are good. Most of today's students only know how to talk about freedom and equality, but they do not pay attention to old virtues, such as loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, and peace. Therefore, now, if you want to be a good student, you should practice a new life, cultivate noble morals, cultivate profound knowledge, exercise a strong physique, develop cooperative habits, cultivate the perfection of inner and outer heart, earnestly study, and strive to be a person, and then you can win glory for the country, seek happiness for the people, and add honor to the ancestors, and be a true, good, and beautiful good student; therefore, I am working hard now, and I want to be a good student in the future.

Biography of a Righteous Dog (17) 184

— By Xin Qing

He never knew what contours and light and shadow were, nor did he know the method of dissection, but he relied on his own talent and perseverance to patiently paint, and finally completed this portrait. The lonely and lonely old woodcutter on the painting is indeed a very good poem, sitting on that dead tree, quietly as if thinking about something. Behind him is a touch of dusk, covering the old man. This painting is of course very rough, and also has many weaknesses; but fortunately, there is a word "true", on which you can see the truth of nature and the truth of art, containing infinite beauty in the bleakness. After Mother Nature finished her work, Bodey often lay quietly here, watching his little master patiently do his work, and he didn't know how many hours he had spent before and after. It knew that Little Nanluo had a hope, which could be said to be not very certain, because he was determined to complete this painting and send it out to participate in the competition, hoping to get an annual bonus of two hundred francs. This competition was held in Angfanru, and all children under the age of eighteen, whether they were students or farmers, as long as they could paint, sent their works made of lead powder and pencil, and the great painters in Sanluo City served as judges, selecting the most talented little painter and giving him a bonus of two hundred francs.

In the spring, summer, and autumn of this year, Little Nanluo perked up his spirits and worked on this painting. If it was successfully completed and won the championship, then he would be one step closer to his self-reliance movement, and his love for that mysterious art would have a kind of ardent emotion.

He kept the secret strictly and did not tell anyone: his grandfather would not understand this matter, and he was estranged from Xiao Ailuo. He only told Bodey everything, and said in a low voice: "I think Luo Bensi will definitely award me the first prize."

All the paintings participating in the competition were limited to being sent on December 1st, and the results of the judging were also scheduled to be announced on the 24th, so if he won the prize, then by Christmas, he could be happy with his old grandfather and Bodey.

On a cold winter day, just as it was dawning, his heart was pounding, sometimes full of hope, sometimes full of fear, putting the painting on the green cart for delivering milk, helped by Bodey, and together they sent it to the town, until the front of that public building. He timidly thought to himself: "Maybe this painting is not worth a penny, who knows?" He left the painting, and he felt it was a risky and unconscious thing. Imagine how a barefoot poor boy who doesn't even know how to read can attract those great painters to look at his childish works?

He happily walked past the cathedral, as if he saw the shadow of the ancient great painter Luo Bensi, very great, very solemn, now in the dark canal, his lips contained a kind smile, as if murmuring: "Don't be afraid! When I was making my painting name in Angfan'er, my heart was also full of courage." Little Nanluo ran home in this cold night, and received infinite comfort.

He had done his best, and the rest was up to God. Originally, he often worshiped the Holy Lord wholeheartedly in the small chapel among the willows and poplars, and established a kind of unshakable faith.

The winter weather had long been extremely cold. That night, they returned home, and it snowed heavily, for several days in a row, completely covering the paths in the village and the fields, and all the small rivers and streams were frozen, and the plains were terribly cold. In such a cold winter, it was indeed a very difficult thing to go out early in the morning to deliver milk. At that time, the sky had not yet dawned, the whole world was pitch black, and they delivered the milk to the quiet town in the darkness.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Industrial Survey

The Sericulture Industry in Changzhou 185

— Ke Fan

"In the fourth month, there is little leisure in the countryside, just finished with sericulture and then transplanting rice seedlings." This spring seems colder than in previous years, but in the rural areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the "busy sericulture" has already begun.

Changzhou is a very important sericulture area in Jiangsu's territory. The annual export of silkworm cocoons is worth hundreds of thousands of yuan; therefore, although sericulture is a rural sideline, it is a large income item in the rural areas here! Here, the silkworm season is divided into two periods, spring and autumn. Each period has 120,000 sheets of silkworm eggs and more than 40,000 loads of cocoons. If each load is calculated at 30 yuan, each period can get more than 100,000 yuan. If the weather is good and the mulberry fields have a bumper harvest, it will be more than this number. However, in the past, the villagers mostly used the old methods of sericulture, which resulted in the quality of the silkworm cocoons being quite inconsistent; and "cuī qīng" (cuī qīng means drying silkworms), which wasted a lot of manpower. Therefore, Changzhou established a sericulture improvement institution two years ago, which is handled by each county in different districts; its nature is to specialize in cultivating sericulture talents and guiding the sericulture industry.

The Changzhou sericulture improvement area is located in the county seat; Benniu, Henglin, Qishuyan, Shu Dai, Dongtang, Xia Yi Bridge, and Li River Bridge, all towns have sericulture guidance centers, specializing in "cuī qīng" and guiding silkworm breeding work. Each center has two or three instructors, mostly students from sericulture specialized schools or graduates of the school, a total of more than forty people, and the monthly expenses are said to be about 2,000 yuan; the office buildings are mostly provided by the "town offices", so there is no need to spend any rent.

The work of these instructors, in short, is a disguised form of "sericulture maids". This kind of work is very heavy, especially when the "cuī qīng" starts. Here, the "cuī qīng" start date is April 7th, but the official "silkworm rack" date is the 10th; it takes ten days from "cuī qīng" to "entering the flat basket" - that is, the bamboo-made flat basket - to complete, and if the weather is warm, it only takes seven days. The temperature of "cuī qīng" is different every day for ten days; the first day is 62 degrees, and then it is increased day by day, until 78 degrees, which is the last day of "incubating the eggs".

There is another room for "cuī qīng". The layout inside is very simple. There is a triangular wooden frame, with bamboo flat baskets placed in each compartment, and an old-fashioned brazier underneath. There is a thermometer hanging on the wall; these few utensils are the "mother body" for nurturing hundreds of millions of small lives. The four walls of the room and the windows are pasted with layers of paper, and not a single breeze can get in; the ground is paved with square bricks, which is convenient for watering, which is what is called "replenishing moisture". The staff in this room cannot leave this place for a single step all day long. The "guideline" for their work is entirely based on the thermometer hanging on the wall; when the weather is cold, they have to burn charcoal to increase the heat in the room, and conversely, they have to water the ground to "replenish moisture" and lower the temperature; they have to pay attention to the rise and fall of the temperature at all times to maintain a balanced state.

On the day when "cuī qīng" starts - the 7th - the local villagers all come to the guidance center to order silkworm eggs. The silkworm eggs are divided into two types: "boxed" and "paper version". The "boxed eggs" are also called "foreign eggs", which is a wooden frame five inches long and three inches wide, with gauze pasted on both sides, shaped like a cigarette case, so it has this name. The "paper version eggs" are a thick piece of paper the size of a calendar card, with twelve circles drawn on it, and each circle is distributed with a number of silkworm eggs, which at first glance looks like a flat globe. The price of these two types of silkworm eggs is uniformly four corners. The guidance center does the "cuī qīng" on behalf of the villagers, without charging extra fees, but if there are too many silkworm eggs, a certain amount of charcoal fee will be charged as appropriate. After the villagers have ordered the silkworm eggs and written their names, they hand over the silkworm eggs to the instructors for "cuī qīng". According to the regulations here, if the number of silkworm eggs exceeds two to eight sheets, the silkworm farmers must send one person to the guidance center to help. If there are more than ten sheets, two people must be sent. The people sent by the silkworm farmers to practice must absolutely follow the instructions of the instructors for all sericulture procedures, such as "cuī qīng", "replenishing moisture", "loading flat baskets", "applying leaves", "going up the mountain" - the cocooning period - etc., all of which are contrary to the old methods. It is said that in the early days of operation, most of the villagers did not understand the benefits of scientific silkworm breeding, and mostly expressed doubts about this method of sericulture, which made a group of instructors speak until their tongues were parched, and they still could not make them believe it, so there were very few people who came to the guidance center to buy eggs; but after a year of factual performance, the general ignorant and ignorant silkworm farmers sighed in admiration. This year, the silkworm farmers were unusually enthusiastic about buying eggs from the guidance center. From the 7th to the 10th, it is said that the entire Changzhou has sold as many as 120,000 sheets of new eggs, which is an unprecedented phenomenon; however, the staff of the guidance centers everywhere are also busy "happy", although there are still silkworm farmers assisting.

The silkworm farmers practice at the guidance center for a maximum of ten days, but if the weather is warm, it only takes about seven days. When the young silkworms "enter the flat basket", they each go back to raise them, and at the same time, the second batch of silkworm farmers for "cuī qīng" also come up. Therefore, although the "cuī qīng" period is stipulated to be ten days, the work of the instructors is twice this number. When all the silkworm farmers' requests for "cuī qīng" are over, the instructors' work is considered to have reached the first step of completion. The beginning of the second step of work is to go to the homes of the silkworm farmers who have been "cuī qīng" by the guidance center to guide the breeding, observe the moisture content of the mulberry leaves, the height of the temperature, and the evolution of the silkworm eggs; these many situations must be filled into the form one by one. This kind of work is more difficult than "cuī qīng", because the residences of the silkworm farmers in each village are extremely remote, and the mountain roads are rugged. Every day, from Village A to Village B or Village C, you have to walk five or six miles or more than ten miles. They have to start from the office at about 6:00 am every day. If they are strong, they can only walk to three or five villages a day; if it rains or blows wind, it is simply exhausting and they can't run to three silkworm farmers. After more than twenty days, they reach the "going up the mountain" period, but the busy work is forced again, because the silkworms "go up the mountain" are mostly only one or two days away. In this short and most-ending period when the work is about to be completed, they simply don't dare to let go of any place easily. Even if they are sometimes unable to spare the time due to time constraints, the general silkworm farmers are unwilling to let the instructors not come to work. Therefore, during this "going up the mountain" period, a group of instructors have all become "fragrant", and the silkworm farmers are willing to spend a lot of money on lavish hospitality, but a group of instructors are busy to the point where they don't even have time to eat. During the "going up the mountain" period, the previous major needs seven days. During this time, the instructors have to inspect the diseased silkworms for the silkworm farmers every day, and guide them to organize the "rice straw" - which is used by the silkworms to "go up the mountain". The so-called rice straw is to cut the rice stalks into lengths of about a foot, divide them into two bundles, and wrap them with grass rope in the middle, shaped similar to "crisp hair flowers", but several times thicker. When the silkworms reach the time to "go up the mountain", they take it and put it on the "rice straw", allowing them to spin silk and bind themselves! The work of the instructors is considered to be fully completed at this point, which takes a total of more than forty days.

The work of the instructors is in the spring and autumn seasons, so their remuneration is also issued on a seasonal basis, simply speaking, it is a contracting system. A new instructor who has just left school gets a salary of 60 yuan per season - including food. If they have two years of experience or have excellent grades in school, they get a salary of 80 to 85 yuan per season. It is said that 40 instructors were sent out by the Changzhou sericulture area this year, and one-third of them are students who have not graduated from sericulture school, and they were sent out by the school to follow up and practice; the salary of these trainees is uniformly 30 yuan per person, and after deducting travel expenses and food, which cost more than ten yuan, the remaining amount must be handed over to the school as school expenses. In addition to receiving regular salaries, it is said that these instructors also have a kind of performance reward, but the amount is not certain.

Sunday Literary Society

On Xiaopinwen (Short Essays) 187

— Ms. Xian

The *xiaopinwen* is the darling of modern literature, beloved by a group of literary figures. Indeed, it possesses an inherent power to be loved. Especially now, most young literary people are learning to write *xiaopinwen*, so its importance is beyond doubt. However, what exactly is the essence of the *xiaopinwen*? This question is probably what every author wants to understand!

What is a *xiaopinwen*? Many scholars in China have discussed it, but it is difficult to find a satisfactory and accurate understanding.

In Western literature, works of this genre are called Essays. Some also use the term "Sketch," as used by Mr. [George] Santayana, as a name for this type of writing. Essay, translated by Mr. Zhou Zuoren as "論文" [thesis] or "美文" [belle-lettres], is not very appropriate. LF. Young once gave the following explanation of literary Essays: "A literary Essay occupies a convenient position between fictional works and rigorous scientific and philosophical treatises. It is suitable for any topic, reported in a pleasant, relaxed, and clear form, and presents a framework for examining an argument. It is a lovable tool for authors to express their thoughts on any subject." Although he explained some of the characteristics of the *xiaopinwen*, his overall understanding is still insufficient.

A more accurate definition would be that of Mr. Xia Mianzun: "From the perspective of external length, short articles of two or three hundred words, or even up to a thousand words, are called *xiaopinwen*. The distinction between long articles and *xiaopinwen* is determined only by external form. Therefore, the content and nature of *xiaopinwen* are entirely free. It can narrate events, contain arguments, express emotions, or describe scenery, without any restrictions. ... *Xiaopinwen* have existed in China since ancient times. For example, the *xiaopinwen* of Su Dongpo are very famous. The common so-called "隨筆" [jottings] can also be regarded as a type of *xiaopinwen*. Recently, *xiaopinwen* have become even more popular in various countries; and the style is very different from what we traditionally called *xiaopinwen*. The current *xiaopinwen* is actually a translation of "Sketch." They generally express real feelings or a part of real life in fragmented writing."

Feng Sanmei also offered a more precise explanation in his lectures on *xiaopinwen*: "The so-called *xiaopinwen* refers to texts with simple content and short form. *Xiaopinwen* can also narrate events and reason, but its essence is mainly the expression of emotion. Intense and profound emotions can create various lengthy masterpieces, but if they are not so intense and also represent a corner of real life, wanting to preserve them from disappearing rashly, then the *xiaopinwen* is truly a supreme tool. Although the form of the *xiaopinwen* is prose, its nature is close to poetry. It cannot be as loose as ordinary writing, nor as compact as general poetry. If there is a middle ground between poetry and prose, besides prose poetry, then it is a new flower in this region."

Mr. Hu Shi also has a few noteworthy words, he said: "Using plain conversation, containing profound meaning, sometimes it seems clumsy, but it is actually humorous." The "滑稽" [clumsy, comical] mentioned here seems to be quite problematic and falls into superficiality. It should be changed to "幽默" [humor] or "諧趣" [wittiness], because humor and wittiness are conditions that a *xiaopinwen* should possess. In summary, we should arrive at the following more perfect conclusion: *Xiaopinwen* is a short article that expresses and critiques a corner or fragment of life's real feelings with concise, humorous, and meaningful words, and lighthearted skill.

The *xiaopinwen* is a secluded realm of humor in the garden of art, not as broad and vast as the ancients said. Mr. Zhong Jingwen once said: "...The ancients seemed to refer to articles of not too long a length when they mentioned *xiaopin*, and their style combined argumentation, prefaces, postscripts, biographies, epitaphs, etc., and the content included descriptions of scenery, narratives, expressions of emotion, and arguments. According to this, it is not much different from ordinary articles, only shorter."

*Xiaopinwen* is not just a short article; it has its own stylistic characteristics. The Japanese writer Hakuson Kuriyagawa said in his book *From the Ivory Tower*: "If it is winter, sit in a comfortable chair next to the heater; if it is summer, wear a bathrobe and sip fragrant tea, casually chatting with good friends, and simply transferring these words to paper is an Essay. As inspiration strikes, one may say some principles that are not too headache-inducing, there are also cold taunts and aphorisms, there is both Humor (滑稽 [comedy]) and Pathos (感奮 [exhilaration]), the topics discussed range from major national and global affairs to trivial matters in the market, critiques of books, news of acquaintances, and recollections of one's past. Whatever comes to mind is freely discussed, relying on the impromptu pen; this is this type of article." This is enough to illustrate the style of *xiaopinwen* and the sources of its subject matter.

Here we must compare *xiaopinwen* with other literary works:

1. *Xiaopinwen* and Poetry. Although *xiaopinwen* often has lyrical expressions, that is the type of *xiaopinwen* that is rich in poetic meaning. But poetry is, after all, not *xiaopinwen*. Poetry relies on rhyme as a necessary condition, while *xiaopinwen* does not.

2. *Xiaopinwen* and Novels. *Xiaopinwen* and novels can be distinguished by their structure and expression methods. After selecting the subject matter, a novel must undergo considerable arrangement, with a strict structure. The characters, background, dialogue, and narration have all undergone a series of considerations, and then they are expressed with economical skill. The *xiaopinwen* is different. As mentioned above, it uses an "impromptu" method to express a corner of life that suits its purpose; its structure cannot be as strict as that of a novel.

3. *Xiaopinwen* and Argumentative Essays. *Xiaopinwen* is sometimes also an argument on matters of reason or imagery. Many *xiaopinwen* use a cold and stern style to target the front of a certain matter of reason, or lightly tap from the side with a tone of cold sarcasm, and readers feel another kind of clear and cold breath assaults their lungs. But *xiaopinwen* is not, after all, an argumentative essay, because it is still based on its impromptu technique and does not have the formal structure that an argumentative essay should have.

4. *Xiaopinwen* and Drama. Sometimes the author of a *xiaopinwen* also uses the form of drama and simple dialogue methods to complete his writing of *xiaopinwen*, but such examples are rare. For example, Ms. Chen Hengzhe's *The Canal and the Yangtze River*, we always regard as a *xiaopinwen* and do not consider it a drama.

5. *Xiaopinwen* and Diaries. Most *xiaopinwen* take the form of casual talk or jottings, but there is a special form! Diaries and letters

Page 23

, also occupy an important position. Mr. Yu Dafu said: Diary literature is a core in literature and a treasure outside the orthodox. The reason why diary *xiaopinwen* are so deeply moving is precisely because they are a revelation of true feelings, without the need for affectation. They are flawless white jade.

6. *Xiaopinwen* and Letters. *Xiaopinwen* in letter form are also treasures in literature. Mr. Zhou Zuoren said that diaries and letters are particularly interesting things in literature because they express the author's personality more clearly than other articles. Ms. Bing Xin's *To Young Readers*, with its gentle and beautiful diction, innocent and rich feelings, many readers love it. As for the *Three Leaves Collection* by Guo Moruo, Tian Han, and Zong Baihua, how do they discuss life's problems? Righteous, magnificent, and melancholic, full of passionate and intense emotions, it is also a very good *xiaopinwen*.

7. *Xiaopinwen* and Prose Poetry. In some cases, there is simply no clear boundary to distinguish between *xiaopinwen* and prose poetry. We know that there are many *xiaopinwen* that contain a lot of poetic meaning, and the structural form is not very different from prose poetry. Kimura Ki said: "It must not be forgotten that prose has been able to develop to this day because it has borrowed a lot from poetry's effort and skill." Kimura Ki once cited an example of the boundary between poetry and prose: all day; from morning to night; from the time when the morning mist hangs until the time when the crickets chirp. can only express the simple state of daily affairs and cannot be regarded as an expression of special thoughts and feelings. expression, one enters another world. It does not directly express the content, but uses hints to allow readers to grasp the content hidden in the bottom of the description. *Xiaopinwen* is suitable for (3) expression. It requires color rendering, rich interest, and literary sentiment. Therefore, we can say that *xiaopinwen* is "poetic prose."

Here we want to discuss the *xiaopinwen*'s contribution to most authors and the estimate of its intrinsic value:

First, the value to the author

A. Cultivating skills—To become a skilled writer, one cannot immediately write long articles or masterpieces. Long articles or masterpieces are more burdensome work. *Xiaopinwen* are easy to find material for and convenient to construct. After a considerable period of practice, skills will naturally become flexible.

B. Expanding thinking—Describing a corner of life from daily life, the author's interest is aroused by the writing of real feelings, and literary ideas are like the clear spring in a secluded valley, endlessly flowing.

C. Increasing the ability to savor life—The ability of literature is to express life, and to critique life. *Xiaopinwen* is also an expression and critique of real life. Therefore, to write *xiaopinwen*, one must savor one's own real life and understand the interest of one's own real life, and then one can express life.

D. Cultivating keen observation!—The expression of literature is the deep excavation of life's transverse heart. We should develop a keen ability to see through life or all levels of society and measure our own ideals.

Second, the estimate of intrinsic value

A. Expansion of self-color—This is not necessarily a cold, rigid, and objective record, but another very strong personal tune is being played.

B. Adherence to fleeting moments—When human thoughts and emotions fleetingly appear, grasp them, and do not let this fleeting sweetness escape from our short *xiaopinwen*.

In short, *xiaopinwen* is not a grand article that carries the Tao, nor is it the groaning of the healthy, but a portrayal of the positive or side of all life, society, and the universe. It is a treasure in the palace of skill.

Commentary

Thinking of the Departure of MacDonald and Herriot 188

— Ji Ren

When the news of MacDonald's defeat in the British election and Herriot's subsequent loss of the leadership of the Radical Socialist Party in France spread, a satirical cartoon was published in a foreign magazine. The cartoon showed MacDonald stepping down in embarrassment, with Herriot carrying an umbrella, following closely behind MacDonald's ass, walking the same path. After seeing such a cartoon, I naturally found it funny, but at the same time, I could not help but admire the artist's flexible mind. He was able to so ruthlessly ridicule the tragic fate of the two politicians in the British and French political arenas who specialized in selling human heads.

MacDonald was originally the leader of the British Labour Party. He had used the power of a part of British workers to serve as prime minister of the Labour cabinet twice. In general, he could be said to be one of the most active figures on the British political stage. But in 1931, when Britain was in unprecedented financial difficulty, MacDonald, for the sake of the security of British imperialism and to try to overcome the financial difficulties, openly left his own Labour Party and colluded with the Conservative Party, snuggling in Baldwin's arms. In this way, of course, he was to be spurned by his Labour Party and ridiculed by a part of the British people who had still held goodwill towards him. As a result, in this British election, he was severely scolded by the voters and was defeated. Although Baldwin pitied him and gave him a position in the current British cabinet, from now on, the political life of this politician who had once been in the limelight was over. His true colors had been fully revealed, and he would no longer be able to deceive the people he had deceived. His fate was only to serve Baldwin for life, or to be abandoned by the British people in the garbage heap, and from then on, disappear without a trace!

As for Herriot, he was also a very famous figure in France. He was originally the leader of the largest party in France—the Radical Socialist Party; he had served as the Prime Minister of the French Cabinet; since 1905, he had begun to serve as the Mayor of Lyon, and has continued to the present. The French call him "King of Mayors"; this can certainly be said to be the most popular figure on the French political stage in recent years. But during the Laval cabinet, he first violated the will of the Radical Socialist Party and supported Laval's unpopular policies, resulting in opposition from his own party and being forced to resign from the position of party leader. This was a manifestation of the first step he took on the path that MacDonald had taken. Recently, the preliminary results of the French parliamentary election were announced, and Herriot, "contrary to expectations," was defeated. It is said that this is "an unprecedented event in French history." Naturally, his fate in this election will only be fully determined in the second round of voting on May 3, but the failure of this primary election is always a lesson that the French people are continuing to give him, and it is always a manifestation of his political status continuing to decline; even if he is luckily elected in the second round of voting, it is only his last struggle, maintaining his remaining political life. However, according to reports, after the failure of the primary election, Herriot has stated that he "now intends to withdraw from politics and will no longer be a candidate for the second round of elections"; if so, then we can say that Herriot is still able to "recognize the times" and can not continue to cling to power when the people are dissatisfied with him. This is better than MacDonald, who has already failed, begging Baldwin to maintain an official position. However, no matter what, the fate of these two figures is always the same.

The same fate encountered by MacDonald and Herriot has given us two important feelings;

First, MacDonald is essentially a reformist and liberal. Such figures can only ease the current struggles of life and cannot take the road forward at all; under certain circumstances, he may even openly do the dirty work of reversing the car. Therefore, when MacDonald can still continue to play a deceptive and easing role, he can still wear the mask of reform and work hard at peaceful preaching; but now, "he can no longer play such an easing role, and the party members he leads have increasingly left him to take the path they should take. Therefore, for the sake of his personal position, he automatically tore off his mask and openly colluded with the Conservative Party to work hard at the work of reversing the car. At the same time, Herriot is also a conservative, middle-of-the-road liberal. Although the Radical Socialist Party he led in the past has the name "radical," it is actually a middle-class party of French citizens. Because France gained many spoils in the last great war, and society was relatively stable, the middle-of-the-road, moderate, and conservative political views of this middle-class French citizens' party—the Radical Socialist Party—gained the support of most French people, making this party the largest party in France, and the leader of this party, Herriot, also became the most prominent figure in French politics. But recently, because of the development of internal and external crises in France, the struggle between the left and right extremes has become sharp, and the middle-of-the-road Radical Socialist Party has gradually lost power. Herriot, who could not even keep up with the tail of the times, would naturally have to retire in this great era of France, and even combine with the most conservative forces. This is inevitable. According to this analysis, we can think that people like MacDonald and Herriot are the most unreliable: in making friends and in social activities, we should secretly guard against them, lest we be sold by them.

Second, MacDonald was once the leader of the British Labour Party, and Herriot was once the leader of the French Radical Socialist Party. Their past political status was given to them by their party, not created by them personally. Therefore, once they betrayed their party's position and violated their party's will, they also lost their inherent power and status. From this, we can further think that people are social and collective animals. The strength of the individual can only grow and be exerted in the group, and therefore the individual's way out can only be found in the group's way out. Whoever leaves his own group and cannot find a new and better group to join, but only goes his own way or relies on others, will only continue to make his soul degenerate and enter a dead end. MacDonald and Herriot's departure from and violation of their political parties cut off their political lives. Gandhi's withdrawal from the Indian national liberation movement quickly lost his prestige among the Indian people. Gu Ruzhen's and others' treason was cursed by the entire Chinese people. ... There are countless examples of this kind.

Celebrity Interview

Mr. Tang Huaiqiu 189

— Xu Xinqin

Anyone who pays attention to China's new drama movement knows the historical value of the South China Society, right? And Tang Huaiqiu, the leading actor and veteran of drama in the South China Society, is someone that anyone would have to call out "I've admired you for a long time." Recently, the "China Traveling Theater Troupe" led by Tang Huaiqiu has returned from North China with honors. After hearing the news, the reporter made a special trip to No. 13 Yingcun, Supheid Road, to visit this Big Brother Tang.

Arriving at Yingcun, I saw a large number of stage sets piled up under the overpass building in the alley. Following the stage sets, I walked to No. 13 in a roundabout way. From outside the door, I heard the sound of reciting lines inside the door, all in a clear Beijing accent. And suddenly, the wild laughter of a middle-aged man came from far and near to the door. At this time, I happened to push the door open, and he almost bumped into me. As soon as I saw him, I shouted in surprise: "I haven't seen you for a long time! Shop..." He excitedly shook my hand: "Ah! Your news is really well-informed. Three or four people have already come to inquire about the news today. Please come in and sit down!"
